  • Zacxh returns from his errands and finds Trynn to make good on his promise to '...find him later and fill him in'

    Zacxh approaches slowly sizing up the skittish little fighter. Then sits down next to him, hands him a slab of mushroom bread and a savory hunk of cheese. After a generous swig of watered down wine from a large wooden cup, he hands that to Trynn as well.

    'Please eat something brother. Your bones poke out of every corner.'

    Zacxh watches like a mother hen until Trynn takes a bite and then begins his report.

    'The man I met in captain Xulleyl’s quarters was none other than the legendary Geldirin, Steward of Nerr’tenden. He is reported to be the best swordsman in all Nerr’tenden. Did you know he is also Sword master of house Nerr’tenden?

'As a slave and a secret one at that, I knew little about him but I have been asking around a bit to find out about him. Apparently he is one of only a very few elves in a lifetime that are elevated to nobility from outside the royal family.' 'He is reported to be a relaxed and friendly sort, and though I could not make out many of the details of his conversation with our captain, he struck me as competent and fair. They seemed to have a comfortable working relationship, and when I entered, he greeted me with warmth and generosity. He even knew my name and hoped I was enjoying my new posting.'

'I must say that, given who he is, I was impressed he had taken the time to know of me.'

'Did you know that Captain Xulleyl is the Chief of Security and Captain of the Guard here in Nerr’tenden? Much has been made of her alleged ill intentions toward us, but I find that notion rather ridiculous. I think it is more likely that she is hoping to build a quiet and powerful unit to extend her power and influence perhaps a bit outside the walls of house Ossund. Personally, I have no problem with that. In fact, I think maybe it was I was born to do.'

'I am a killer Trynn, only that. I killed to defend my fallen house, I have killed for the sport of cruel masters, and now I kill for house Ossund... Well... For Captain X at least... At first I rebelled against this fate. Now I embrace it. If my life has a greater purpose I do not know it, so all I have is this;

I live only for the day, for the adventure and enjoyment it can bring me, and for my friends. That means you and a few others perhaps. Everyone else... Well they can either stay out of my way or die senselessly on my blade as so many have before. My loyalty to you comes from my knowledge that you will act to keep me safe and that we are cut from a similar cloth. Which brings me to this next question. I will ask it so as to better understand why you are so cowed by mere elves as though they were divine.'

'What is it that binds you. Why are you so afraid. What does The Captain hold over you which makes you fear her so. Surely it is not death. Slaves like us have given in to their pain and their mortality long hence. Hell! That surrender is the greatest gift I have ever received. If I had known what they brought, I would have embraced each lash as a treasure.'

Zacxh looks at the mangled flesh of his arm and grins, lost in thought a moment.

Gently. 'Anyhow... What is it Trynn? What holds you back? Who can I kill for you to help restore some of your fire? We are all dead men walking, at least we can wear a smile in our final days.'

  • The smile Zacxh forces onto his so lifeless face is not at all

convincing.

Trynn stares quietly at Zacxh for a long minute, then shrugs as if to say, why not?

"I believe you may be the first elf I think I can trust, Zacxh. It is not myself that I fear for. It is not death that I fear.

There *is* a plot against House Oussund. Whether it be a full-fledged movement or just a small conspiracy I cannot say, but it is real.

And I am part of it.

No, not what you think. I am no traitor. They have ensnared me against my will. You see, they poisoned me. A slow acting agent that if untreated will slowly drive the victim mad, stark raving mad.

But there is an antidote. A treatment. I have been taking it but my supply is running low, so I have been rationing it. Sometime after a couple days of going without, I begin to act... erratic. That's what was going on in the mines, Zacxh. I had gone three days letting the madness advance without taking the antidote.

The problem is that if I go too long, I may not come back. I know there is a limit I just don't know how far it goes.

But it's more than just a poison. The antidote is a catalyst, and when combined with a third substance (which is unknown to me), it works as a drug that makes me utterly compliant. Thus I am their tool. Whenever they want me to perform a task in service to their traitorous schemes, they simply introduce the drug. It could be a powder, an incense, something in my food or drink. I don't know. (and thus my initial reaction to Valron messing with our food). But once I'm drugged, it's a simple matter for them to give me instructions. The effect lasts for a day or two.

Mostly they have only asked me for information or small little tasks, such as leaving a certain door unlocked or passing a notes anonymously.

But with this 'fake death' business and the Spidergaurd, I'm in a precarious position. A cleric was killed during my "fake death". If the Oussund priestesses find out I'm really alive, and if my condition comes to light, it will be a very bad day. Not for me mind you. I do not fear their punishments, but I fear for my mother."

Trynn sighs loudly. "Maybe I should start at the beginning".

My parents were destroyed by House Oussund during a purge of traitors.

They tried to take us in our sleep, and but for a loyal friend who came to warn us of the coming violence, they would have succeeded. A quick, raspy scratch outside our residence. A scrape of stone upon stone. Two scrapes. Pause. Two scrapes more.

My father leaped to his feat in an instant, as if he had been waiting for that sound.

He trembled visibly, whether from adrenaline or fear I could not tell. But he whispered fiercely to my mother as quiet footsteps retreated from our door. "We are betrayed!"

Those words have haunted me ever since, and I am still to be convinced that he was really a traitor to House Oussund. He was betrayed. Why else would he say as much when there was no one of influence to hear it?

And there is one other piece of evidence in his favor. It is said that blood runs true, and the sins and virtues of the parents are passed on to the children. But if blood runs true then my parents were no traitors, for I am loyal to House Oussund.

That dark day of the purge, my parents were luckier than some others. They got a warning from a loyal friend at least.

I remember my father hissing desperately at us to "Go!" and then turning to face the intruders we could already hear approaching, his rapier held ready.

Unlike the clerics and nobles of the highborn, my parents held genuine affection for each other. I will never forget how they paused, how she squeezed his hand briefly before whisking me out and into the secret escape route they had planned. I've never seen a highborn so much as smile at a male but my mother stopped and burned precious seconds to squeeze his hand, knowing he was doomed.

We ran.

As we fled I could hear the sounds of battle, strange sounds to my young ears. The sounds of metal biting into flesh, of blood splattering a floor, the sounds of my father dying in his attempt to give us precious minutes for our escape.

We survived for weeks. First we hid outside of Dolthgurdar. My parents had secured hidden supplies for just this occasion. We moved each day, recovering food and water from secret caches out in rarely travelled tunnels. My mother spoke to me of House intrigues, of factions and of religion, of things like prestige and jealousy and power. I was too young to understand it all but I understood the lessons behind it. I learned that the House was not to be crossed. It was enough to even be mistaken for an enemy. House Oussand would find you and crush you.

Eventually we returned in secret to her cousin's house. The search was still on and she knew that she couldn't hide forever. She arranged a deal to give up in return for sparing me and they accepted. She was indentured for a hundred years and I was made a slave of the clerics. It was a marvelously successful outcome for us compared to what they had intended of course. All thanks to my father, who sacrificed himself to give us a brief moment to run.

I remember that she squeezed my hand as they took me away forever. She told me, "this is your new mother now," but I knew she didn't mean it. It could never be true. Even my loyalty to House Oussund could waver if she asked it. But she didn't ask it, and that is but more evidence to me that she was not a traitor. Since then I have seen her only a handful of times. Secret meetings arranged for short moments in time, a risk worth taking.

I was assigned as the personal slave of a young cleric. She took on the role of a mother, only very different from my own. Domineering, harsh and unforgiving. I was whipped when I did wrong, rewarded when I groveled. She taught me what I needed to learn. I am thankful to her for that.

....

I later learned they had executed my father, then revived his corpse to work as a mindless automaton scout in the territories threatened by psionic races. I do not blame the Matriarch for this. She acted on what information she had. It is only natural to crush your enemies while you still can, and to make future enemies think twice about the consequences they will face.

Over the years it became apparent I was gifted with unusual strength and agility, so my "mother" had me trained to dance for their ceremonies and gatherings.

I loved it. It was a release, an escape from my life as a slave. When I danced, I was free to move how I wanted, to be my own agent. Every waking moment of my day and night, every action every thought, were under complete control of my cleric "mother" except for when I danced. My dancing was very good. She rewarded me with lighter duties; I was not required to work the kitchens anymore. But she was still liberal with the lash when it was warranted.

It was arranged for me to be trained as a bodyguard, and so they sent me to an old retired guard with bad eyesight name Ghuan'Diirn, now living in peace near the outskirts of Dolthgurdar. The best part of my training was the long walks from the slave quarters to his residence. It was a kind of freedom, wandering the streets, witnessing the normal lives of Dolthgurdar. The clerics had no fear of me running away. They could find me with ease, and we all knew that my indentured mother would be punished for any of my failures. What they didn't know was that my loyalty to her transcended even my fear of them. I was able to arrange secret meetings with her more frequently. They were brief and innocent, usually just a quiet moment over tea while she asked me about my life with a mother's concern.

If the best part of my day was walking to meet with Ghuan, the hardest part of my day was walking home. The training left me beaten and exhausted. His training was brutal, but not cruel. He was demanding, but not vindictive. He may have been old, but he was certainly not weak. My training was as much mental as physical. He trained me to endure, to suffer, to have a mental discipline that would serve me for any challenge.

We spent hours balancing with heavy weights, sparring upside down suspended from ropes, running courses blindfolded, fighting with hands numbed from ice, boxing barefoot on a floor strewn with sharp rocks, and more. Every day was a new pain. I lived with the pain. Every strike, every hold, every excercise was agony. I limped home every day. I resented much of it at the time, but it made me strong.

And he was able to spot my latency when no one else had. He taught me to look into myself, to dig deep from my own psychic will when I felt I had nothing left. I didn't quite understand what he meant but I tried.

I could feel it tantalizingly near, a oneness of body and mind that would surely lend me strength.

He warned me not to tell the clerics of all we practiced. I found this odd, and scary, but I did as he instructed. As far as they were concerned, an old decrepit monk was teaching me some basics, that is all.

And then came the day that I died.

The priestess came into my quarters without knocking or even looking at me.At first, I thought it was my death, that they had discovered my condition and my life was forfeit.

She was reading something in her hands and paused just long enough to snap at me. "You will accompany me as the Second. Now." And she left. She never even looked up. Her name was Shaille, but I only knew that because of overhearing conversations amongst the other slaves.

So, I was to be given my first assignment as a bodyguard to Lolth's chosen. Nearly an honor. Mostly just an opportunity to be punished for failure. That much I understood. I secured my weapons and met them out front, the cleric with her First. He eyed me with disdain and dislike. The bodyguards are constantly shifted around in rank and privilege, causing jealousy and intense competition. The clerics like it that way of course. They say it brings out the best.

"We are to meet at a rendezvous point where I will confer with someone. You of course shall remember nothing if asked. That is your role. Watch, protect, sacrifice." And she turned on her heel.

The First walked in front, and I in back. She led us out of Dolthgurdar, into caves and tunnels.

I still suspected this was all related to my poisoned condition and possibly even a ruse to flush me out. I began to worry that she was part of the group who had poisoned me! Hoping that my nerves were not betraying me, I focused on my inner will, as Ghuan had taught me.

They struck quickly and the cleric was down before I could even react. I saw the First draw his sword and then darkness descended as I fumbled with my whip. Damn! Then a loud cracking clap of sound nearly deafened me followed by a gurgling gasp from the First. I had no idea what to do. I turned to retreat and at least get out of the globe of darkness. That is when something struck my head and I was out, the smell of ozone the last thing I remembered.

I awoke slowly. Someone was dragging me along the floor, holding my armpits and pulling me from behind. Between my two feet, I could see three figures lying on the floor. The cleric, and the First, and another figure, all charred beyond recognition. Something odd..... something not >quite right... the third figure was dressed and outfitted just like me! >The same gear, and the same build, everything. A charred husk. Was I dead?

"He wakes". A figure crouched in my view, putting a small vial in my hand. "They will come to clean up. Stay quiet, they will not find you. Drink this when you are ready to move again." Then something heavy was slipped into my pocket. "Read this when you wake. Your masters will think you dead, so be wary". I drifted off, agony pulsing across my skull. My masters would think me dead, and so would Mother. I wished she could squeeze my hand one more time.

I finally woke again to the sounds of angry voices as they cleaned up the bodies and searched for clues. I had been stuffed into a crevasse down a side passage. I was cramped and hurt and thirsty, but alive. I waited in discomfort until they left.

I now make my way to the Crystal Gate, as the note instructed. What choice do I have? I have failed the clerics. My first assignment an utter failure. Even if I went back, too much is at stake. My poisoned condition would surely come to light, my terrible failure in my first assignment. A dead priestess. They would be forced to assume I am a traitor.

And who is behind this latest turn for me? Is it the poisoners? Or is it the clerics testing my loyalty? Or someone else entirely? I have no choice but to see where this goes. I can trust no one...

Trynn looks up after this long winded tale, eyeing Zacxh carefully.

"So you see now? I'm in a bad spot, and it's of utmost importance to me to determine who is behind this poisoning of my mind. And also it is paramount that no one in Dolthgurdar discover that I yet live. It is my mother's life at stake. I know that for many elves, bonds of loyalty are considered weak, especially family bonds, but I am unique. I would give anything for her. And I find loyalty to be a great strength.

And you have mine to do with as you see fit, sir"

Zacxh takes in the story with his typical dead eyed stare. Once it is completed, the disfigured pit fighter sits motionless as a stone, either asleep behind those faraway eyes, or perhaps not there at all.

Just as Trynn begins to think himself a fool for divulging so much, Zacxh finally moves. And quickly. His hand darts out like a viper's and catches Trynn by the throat. His razor sharp dagger appears in the other hand and in an instant Trynn realizes he has made a huge mistake. Zacxh holds him there a moment before a frightening smile melts through his normally expressionless face.

Then he speaks.

"I believe I understand your problem now. Our employers did not do nearly a complete enough job in killing you. Well, for death you so desperately need, you have come to exactly the right elf."

Zacxh raises his gleaming blade and holds it in front of Trynn’s eye. He watches Trynn’s look of horror mix with resolve.

"Oh. huh hu hagh!"

The laugh which erupts from Zacxh's throat seems alien and seldom used.

"Oh, no Trynn I think you misunderstand. I am not going to kill you. No. I am going to horribly wound and disfigure you. With your permission of course."

"You need a new face... perhaps a new voice too. A face like mine brother."

Zacxh lets Trynn go to gesture at his scarred and mangled countenance.

"Of course it is only if you will it."

"My dead mother, looking directly into my eye from the very pit of hell itself would never recognize me. We need to give you a makeover, and my little friend here may be just the stylist you have been in need of." (Zacxh holds up his knife)

"We change your face and your name so 'Trynn' is no more. Then we change your mind into a fortress that no poison can penetrate. Then, and this is where I put *my*life into *your* hands, for my next words are dangerously spoken... Then we kill every priestess who ever knew you existed and anyone who they might have told."

Zacxh rubs his horrible hand across his horrible face.

"Have I ever told you that I really have no love of the priestesses of house Oussund? Oh don't look so shocked. This is not a treason, well... not a really vile one anyhow.(Zacxh grins) Actually, I hate all of Lolth’s bitches equally regardless of their family name... But I digress. We were discussing you not me."

"I am not an over clever elf, but even I can see you need a completely new identity. So, what do you say, shall we get started brother?"

Trynn politely declined the offer.

  • A few days after the splitting of loot.... Trynn approaches Zacxh and Inarra one morning after we have enjoyed our breakfasts.

"Shall we give this a try? I've taken the liberty of preparing an area of the training cavern for my usual training methods. Let's see what we can learn from other."

  • Trynn leads you two into the training area where there is a section near the back which he has prepared.

    "My approach has always been about mind body discipline. I have found that strength of mind has translated into the strength of body for me. By testing my mind's limits to pain, I am able to push through a barrier of sorts and that is when I enjoy a oneness of mind and body that lend me strength in battle.> Zacxh, this story you have about becoming a bear. It sounds like we're both on the path to discovering a similar power. It would be interesting to see how you have furthered this knowledge for yourself. But first, let me show you how I learned to mentally bolster my own vigor during battle and take more injury than would normally be possible. Inarra, this will be far different than you are used to I am sure."

    You see that a good 15' foot square of floor near the wall has been strewn with jagged bits and pieces of chipped rock.

    Trynn squats and removes his thin leather boots, still the standard slave-issue footwear he arrived at Nerr’tenden with.

    Barefoot, he bounces up and down, shaking his arms and loosening up like an athlete about to enter the ring. He mumbles to himself with a strange accent: "dishiling, dishiling"> Suddenly, he sprints for the wall, speeding barefoot over the layer of sharp stone chips and then almost immediately pulls up, favoring one foot. He curses to himself.

    "By Lolth's stinky ass!".

    He slowly walks back, methodically stepping back to where he started using equally spaced paces. He shakes his head. "The goal is to hit that wall at full speed but I winced and slowed up, so I must start over. My discipline failed to hold." His feet trail lines of blood.

    Pausing to breathe and focus, he closes his eyes and mumbles again to himself: "dishiling, dishiling".

    He sprints again over the painful floor at full speed, blood spattering lightly off his feet as he flies toward to the stone wall and just before colliding you see a thin misty aura appear over his skin. He hits face first at full speed, and remains upright. He bounces off and staggers back, totally unhurt. The misty aura has lessened noticeably.

    "Looks like I've still got it down. It worked. It took me six weeks to get it right last time. It's good to know that my skills are becoming more reliable....

    Trynn glances off to the side and you both notice two ropes attached to the ceiling and hanging down to the floor. Trynn grins. "Ready for more?"

  • Zacxh regards Trynn blankly as usual. He stares a moment then with perfect deadpan timing looks at Inarra...

    'Dishiling, dishiling... Hmm!'

His eyes don't flicker, he doesn't blink and his voice is as passionless as that of a golem, but something about him... It’s impossible to say what, assures you that beneath his deadened exterior he laughing uncontrollably.

  • 'Trynn indeed your method is quite different than mine. Where you inflict immediate physical pain upon yourself my... History makes that unnecessary. I retreat to a sort of fortress in my mind. I am there now in fact. There are places so dark and so angry within my soul that my thoughts can never go there. Memories of dead friends, of humiliation, and of the beatings... Yes all those beatings...'

    Zacxh is lost in a memory for a moment.

    'There is power... and protection held within all that pain. I merely focus my thought in a safe, pain free and happy place within my mind and fling open the securely held doors to all those horrors.' 'I can almost hear those horrible and powerful memories run through the unsecured portions of my head and my body reacts. It is if I become a coach to my body asking it to do things I would fear. The anger within it drives it well beyond what I could ever hope to consciously will. It is only the fury of my unconscious mind that gives my body wings.

    'I find that now, as I fight for my own ends and according to my own desires, those furies within are not dissipating as I had thought they might, but rather they are intensifying... Gaining confidence if you will.'

    'It is my fear and memory of so many injuries which makes me immune to pain and some damage. My loathing to be cut which is somehow making my skin as iron.'

    'I think it is a more hidden aversion to weakness which changed me that night...'

    Zacxh closes his eyes a moment. A span of a minute passes, then without warning his arms indeed grow. They transform into those of an ogre and even take a greenish hue. He looks as if he could crush a diamond in his impossibly strong grip.

    It only lasts a minute. The arms fade to normal and a tear rolls down Zacxh’s horrible cheek.

    'I will need some time before I can open that door again. It is...painful in a different sort of way.'

    'I envy you your torn feet Trynn'

Trynn lays a hand on Zacxh's shoulder.

"Zacxh, you are the strongest elf I have ever encountered. I'm not talking about your prowess. I have not doubt that those dark days are long behind you now. Great things are in store for you, sir. Look around you. Despite the tensions in the guard, you have already earned much loyalty from valuable allies. You did this by simply being who you are. You have more power than you think. You have earned the envy and enmity of a powerful lieutenant in the House guard! An oppressed and exploited pit fighter no longer. You have already left your past behind, you just don’t realize it yet. Yours will be a fate of both glory and peace I think."

End emails

Zacxh meditated on Trynn's words all that night. He realized that he had been so untrusting in his cruel fate that he turned his back on his possible role as leader of the guard. The more he thought about it, the more the notion began to grow on him. Certainly he was not as handsome and polished as Valron, nor as smooth and convincing a speaker as Inarra. But he was actually fairly happy with the role he had played in planting the seeds of unity within the guard.

Kadyel had again approached Zacxh and stated her ambitions to lead, but Zacxh well knew the reticence that the others were feeling toward her. Valron feared her underhanded dealings, Trynn distrusted her tactical judgement, and though Kadyel stated her belief that the Captain wanted her to lead, Zacxh remembered the look on Xulleyl's face after Kadyell had nearly killed her with that poorly aimed fireball. No, Zacxh did not believe the Captain was grooming Kadyell for command. Even tight lipped Nal had twice commended Zacxh and affirmed his confidence in his leadership.

So Zacxh pondered awhile who might be destined to take the reins of command from him.

Nal was too tight lipped. Trynn was too skittish and perhaps insane. Inarra seemed disaffected and not even convinced the guard needed a leader. Sorn might do, but had no tactical sense and had shown a fairly self centered opinion toward treasure and wealth which would surely be devisive. Valron was firm and steady, also charismatic, but his years of service as a guard seemed to have made him content to follow rather than lead. Len we seemed content to watch and participate, but he never seemed to show any drive to take over and lead the fight.

Zacxh pondered the problem for awhile longer then came to a decision. He would take charge. It needed to be done. He would not announce it as such, but nevertheless he decided to just step in and do the job. He decided to let the Spiderguard eventually decide that he was their servant as well as their center.

Having made the decision, Zacxh's mind jumped into high gear. he had work to do.

Over the next few days, Zacxh served as best he could. He ventured alone back into the mines and hired some of the under utilized miners there to haul every bit of useful equipment out of the storerooms and bring it to the Spider Barracks. He arrainged it around the common room for possible furture use. He also had a heavy bar constructed and affixed to both entrances to secure the barracks.

With the other arms provisions and furnishings, Zacxh brought a large table to the center of the common area and carved a rough spider into its surface. He arranged eight chairs around it and scribed only two of the eight legs. One for both of the party wearing Captain Xulleyls pin.

He asked for each Spiderguard to scribe a symbol in the table and pick a nickname to help hide their identity from the world. For himself he chose 'The Knife'. Nal became 'Teeth', Kadyell became 'Kaballa,' Valron 'Earthquake,' Trynn 'Loyal Phoenix.' Sorn, inarra, and Len we did not immediatly pick names but seemed to be giving the matter some thought.

He arrainged for training in sworsmanship. Lt Ardul was replaced by the other Lieutenent in that capacity. After each session he debriefed his guard and slowly they built up some tactical formations and hand signals.

Weeks passed and he saw some progress. The Guard seemed more cohesive and willing to try and work as a unit in combat. Zacxh felt the beginnings of pride in his fledgling unit and looked forward to their next test.

He didn't have to wait long.

ChapterNine

Chapter Nine: Basking in the afterglow

Zacxh finished his bath quickly. Certainly The meeting between Xulleyl and Valron’s aunt would conclude quickly and Zacxh did not want to upset his captain by being absent when called to duty. He toweled off quickly and began to dress when he realized how badly damaged his fine silk shirt and uniform cloak was from the fire. Zacxh borrowed a brush from the bath master and used it to scrub out and sanitize his beautiful leather armor. After a few minutes of work, the finely wrought stuff began to shine. He discarded his ruined shirt and cloak and dressed minimally in only buffed leather for his return to the barracks. A tip to the bath attendant and he was on his way, much refreshed.

Something seemed missing as Zacxh trekked through the courtyard. It took only a moment to realize that the screaming had stopped. Zacxh looked to see Anthadax absently examine the bodies of two mages and then wander off in his creepy disinterested way.

Zacxh moved quickly. He grabbed up the two bodies of the mages trying hard to appear as part of the general working party straightening up after the battle. He hauled the dead weight bodies effortlessly around a corner and into a discreet location to strip them of valuables. He found some interesting possibly magical trinkets for Sorn and a beautiful dagger for himself and was about to abandon the corpses when he realized one was not actually dead.

Anthadax had not bothered to kill this one, none the less his destruction of the elf was complete. Zacxh looked into the elf’s eyes. There was nothing to be found there. Zacxh knew the symptom well. In his time as a slave occasionally an elf would receive the 'gift' of mercy after having endured torture beyond bearing. The mind was shattered and even if sensibility was restored, the elf would become a shattered broken soul, or worse a nightmare tortured monster hell bent on a mix of revenge and self destruction.

Zacxh examined the trappings of this one. A picture of this elf emerged from his possessions. He was a mage of some promise but still young in his art. He might have one day become something worthwhile, but now, with this deep psychological wound... This poor soul was lost.

Zacxh imagined two possibilities. He saw in his mind the mage mentally crippled, carrying water from the Orlylyl well to the amusement of sneering warriors. The other possibility was much worse. He envisioned him twisted and obscene, pouring over the light of a dim candle researching twisted arcana in an ultimately fruitless quest for power and revenge. never again would he allow himself to fall victim to one more powerful. Never would he allow himself to be so shamed.

Either way this elf was destroyed. Anthadax knew his powers well.

Zacxh leaned in and administered one last test.

'Elf my name Zacxh and I am going to kill you unless you ask otherwise.'

Nothing. The eyes stared thoughtlessly ahead from a sagging face.

Zacxh sighed and put his hand over the mages nose and mouth. As the mage began to turn blue, Zacxh remembered something he had overheard someone once say about not wanting to be sustained if her were wounded in battle in such a way as to become simple.

Normally, there would be some struggle as the elf’s subconscious survival mechanism kicked in to preserve what was left. Even that was destroyed or subverted by the torture. The mage died without a twitch.

Zacxh waited a moment lost in thought , then picked up the bodies and brought them to the front gates. He brushed past Ardul's guards and strode unconcerned to the corporal of the Orlylyl troop waiting outside.

'I believe these are yours. I apologize for having detained them while they were interrogated by our mage. Though the 'discussion' went on for awhile, I do not believe that they really had much to say.'

There was a slight chuckle from one of Ardul's troop. Zacxh was pleased that for once, his humor had found an appreciative ear. He spun on his heel and returned to the Spiderguard barracks.

Zacxh changed into one of his fine black silk shirts and began to work on maintaining his weapons and gear. He worked ritualistically, shining and oiling and polishing everything to a new and gleaming sheen of oil and lightly fragranced sweat. Finally satisfied, he turned his attention to the sack of gear he had salvaged on the battlefield. He was just beginning the task of sorting it into the growing inventory arrayed about the main chamber of the Spiderguard barracks when a knock came at the chamber door. Everyone in the room immediately recognized it as the knock of Captain Xulleyl. Chairs scraped and bodies shuffled to attention as the door opened. Nal seemed to quickly conceal something he was working on as the chamber door flung open.

The Captain, Steward, and Orlylyl priestess marched in. Captain Xulleyl was about to speak but the Priestess rudely blurted in a voice just short of rage.

'I Have discussed the situation with your Captain here and we have decided to investigate this matter fully.

Before I go, I want to see each of you clearly. We *will* meet again... so stand and state your name that I may mark you.'

Each Spiderguard stood and stated their name around the room, until the priestess's gaze fell upon Zacxh.

'They call me The Knife priestess.' Zacxh cared little for her petty display of power.

She Seethed at the unsatisfactory answer.

'Well I refuse to call you that. What is your name slave?'

Zacxh decided to save this fight for another day.

'Zacxh.'

She leered a moment and continued around the room. Once her interrogation was complete, she departed. Zacxh felt a surge of resentment in her presumption. He suddenly felt ashamed that he had not defied her more resolutely, if not for his own sake, then at least to show Trynn that such nonsense should not be tolerated.

Zacxh understood the exercise well. By asserting herself such deep within the enclave of her enemy, she established a hold everyone present.

Captain Xulleyl showed her the door and turned to address the party.

'Apparently she thinks she can toss around orders here...'

'Apparently she is correct' Zacxh mumbled well under his breath.

Captain Xulleyl issued orders and solicited a few questions then departed. The guard was to resume mining operations and be available for any ops that the Captain dreamed up in the meantime.

Zacxh went to the practice arena and ran through his exercises then returned to his room to rest for the evening.

He sat down and leaned back on the cool stone of the small chamber still shared with Valron. He could feel the subtle vibrations of steam and hot water which ran throughout the deep stone of the Underdark, and knew that somewhere far above, those movements were shepherded by the motions of a huge 'flying stone' which dominated the endless openness of sky above the heads of groveling burn elves. Gnomish scholars purportedly had a simple physical answer about how and why the flight of this alleged rock caused the Underdark to rhythmically breath its titanic surges of steam, water and magma, but of course the daughters of Loth claimed that it was merely 'the will of the spider queen.' Zacxh was sure the gnomes and dwarves and burn races all had similar bogus explanations dealing with their own gods and heroes. The walls, meanwhile, breathed on, warming and cooling, belching steam and fire and throbbing with the uncanny regularity that they would doubtless continue to exhibit long after the races of drow and man and the will of Loth were nothing more than forgotten legend.

The vibrations of the flow had slowed to a near crawl, and the color of the walls here were just cooling. It must be early yet, too early to rest again, but Zacxh closed his eyes anyway and tried to blink away the memory of that poor mage screaming himself mad.

Zacxh rested throughout the ebb, and halfway through another. He came to his senses stiff and haunted by visions of Anthadax, so he grabbed a heavy and battered practice sword and spent some time panting and sweating out the herbs of the bathhouse in the practice arena. He returned to the barracks refreshed and loose.

Slowly the main barracks filled with elves, and without much fuss, the Spiderguard gathered the equipment and rations needed to camp out in the mines for a few days and made the hour long trek to the dig, accompanied of course by Nal's troop of conscripts.

Despite the fact that Zacxh had repeatedly reminded the conscripts that they answered to Valron, they defaulted in their requests for guidance to Nal. Zacxh couldn't find a real objection to that, but somehow it still bothered him. He wondered if Nal might not use them in an objectionable way, all too well remembering having to fight through the little unit to get to Kadyel. Zacxh wondered if that battle might not one day be rejoined. The three who he had battered through that day were standing nearby and Zacxh noticed that they tended not to meet his eye and give him a wide berth.

Valron and Nal took charge of the mining outpost security and Zacxh conferred with his recently selected foreman to ensure all was progressing well. Before long the three units, miners, conscripts, and the Spiderguard were all settled comfortably in. The site was secure and well protected. At Zacxh's suggestion, Nal sent a few local patrols out to ensure privacy. It seemed just a matter of time before the mineral was uncovered. Once that happened, the shit would surely hit the fan so Zacxh resolved to gain the confidence of the troops and miners, explore the possibilities of his ever growing mental power and meditate about the meaning of 'honor.'

Several days passes with not much to do, so each shift change, Zacxh started a dice game with the objective of loosing a lot of money to engender trust and reduce anxiety among the troops. He knew that he had a mostly unwarranted reputation for brutality and instability. With luck familiarity would reduce that impression. Zacxh really wanted to be able to rely on these elves in a pinch.

Some time later a commotion came from the guard post outside the secret door to the mine entrance which Zacxh and the others moved to investigate. When they arrived at the security outpost, they found Fals the shureken slinger standing opposed by nervous conscripts. Fals appeared to be injured by a few wicked looking whip marks and stood with hands held wide as if to show he was unarmed. The idea of an unarmed member of Loth's fang was of course ludicrous but the stance was at least unthreatening.

Fals explained that he had been expelled from his house and that he had decided to come to the only safe haven he knew. Valron. The story was of course highly suspect to Zacxh, but he held his tongue to see what would come.

To show his good faith, Fals pointed out one of Nal's conscripts and accused him of being a priest. The accusation was as ridiculous as it was terrifying. Zacxh's interest was immediately piqued. He so very hoped to make the acquaintance of an actual priest that he could hardly contain himself. He knew his desire was a heresy that would be punishable by death, but he would love to speak theology to this elf and maybe learn some hidden truths about horrible Loth. If anyone would know them, surely it would be a priest. Loth had no priests of her own, certainly not secret ones traveling as mercenaries so if the accusation was true, Zacxh might have found for himself an interesting conversation.

Needless to say the room erupted. once the dust settled the 'priest' was manacled and interrogated and Fals, who preferred to be called Flick now that her defenses were dropped, was sitting and chatting up Trynn. He was obviously entranced by the beauty and power of his once and future enemy.

In the end of course the 'priest' confessed to heresy and abominations of any sort demanded to avoid being further questioned by Nal and his cruel blade. Zacxh sadly concluded that the poor elf was probably innocent of any priestlyness but he volunteered to make a run to Nerr’tenden anyhow to inform Xulleyl of current events. The run would do him good.

Zacxh set out at an invigorating pace and was well exercised by the time he arrived panting at Xulleyl's door. He knocked and entered when beckoned to find his timing was poor. Xulleyl was in conference with the Steward and Priestess. They all looked at him as if patronizing a child who interrupts the adults at dinner.

The steward made a civil greeting and Xulleyl bade Zach speak.

'Good evening honored Priestess and Steward. I have come to report to my Captain of minor events transpiring in the mines, but clearly I interrupt. You have my deep apology, and I shall return when you have concluded your business.'

The steward's voice was pleasant but insistent. ' Nonsense Zacxh, speak your report. I'm sure we are all interested to hear of your adventures in the mine.'

'Yes. Speak worm.' The priestess was anything but pleasant. Zacxh remembered her cruelty in beating a soup bearer to death, and momentarily envisioned her gouting blood on the end of his sword.

'Certainly honored Priestess, though I fear my report is of little interest. We have captured a spy in the mines. She has made strange accusations of an elf in our company claiming that he is a priest.'

The Loth priestess sprang to her feet and approached in a fury.

'You fool! How could you suppose this was not of the gravest interest to me?!' The priestess was furious and brought her full force of presence to bear. Zacxh dove into his mental fortress and acted cowed to avoid a beating, but continued his pleasing fantasy of her gouting ichors through the mouth.

'Of course oh dread Priestess. How stupid of me. I merely thought it best to gain the captain's opinion on the matter as certainly the accusation is baseless untrue. Such an elf is the stuff of bedtime stories and certainly cannot truly exist.'

The priestess, as always, was livid. but Zacxh hoped she would trip up and confirm the unlikely existence of such a being.

'Stupid male. This is a matter for the church not a pack of ignorant slaves and peons.'

Zacxh saw the priestess anew. She was more than just unstable, she was another piece of damaged goods. Her actions were motivated by more than the needs of order and discipline. She too was insane. Another victim of Loth’s twisted dominion.

Zacxh found himself leading the three lords of Nerr’tenden toward the mines. He cared little for the safety of the priestess, but strode out to point position in order to buffer the Steward and Xulleyl form attack. Part of him believed the whole thing to be a trap designed to lure all the power players of Nerr’tenden out from behind it's gates. He stole a word with his Captain.

'Sir perhaps this a trap designed get all our eggs in one basket...'

Xulleyl looked unconcerned. She cast a rare grin upon Zacxh. 'Not eggs Zacxh. Dragons.'

Zacxh could not suppress a smile and jogged back to his position at the point. As usual, the Captain had a good point.

The scene back at the mining checkpoint was a bit unsettling. Flick and Trynn sat conversing like old lovers. Nal had a wicked look on his face. Valron was visibly upset about something, and the priest had the look of someone about to be thrown into a volcano. His eyes were wide and terrified, his skin pale and clammy, and his manacled hands looked blue and bloodless as they clasped a fresh wound on his thigh. He was clearly going into shock.

The arrival of Zacxh's entourage caused a stir among the conscripts, but the Spiderguard was suspiciously unsurprised; clearly forewarned. Inarra probably had used her psionic arts of foresee the arrival. The 'priest' however could not have been more surprised and terrified if a black dragon had pranced in. His fear was well justified.

Without preamble, the priestess strode up and bashed him fatally to the side of the head with a battered, well used mace. She then bent down to perform some dark prayer on him. She was interrupted, perhaps for the first time in her life. Incredibly, it was Nal.

"Wait!' The look on his face was a mixture of resolve and the realization that he had perhaps just uttered his own death sentence.

The priestess looked at him coolly and finished her prayer. The 'priest's' body healed some and he gasped a rattling breath. The priestess stood and walked like a panther toward Nal. He backpedaled.

'My sincerest apology priestess, I only though that you should hear of my interrogations of this elf before he was put to death. I have administered a thorough investigation upon him, and in my opinion he is no priest...'

The priestess spoke with obvious menace in a voice which brought a cascade of dust from the the unsteady mining rafters above.

'You will never question my actions again! No *male* may presume to interrupt me! Ever!'

She turned from Nal and addressed everyone and no one.

'The fate of this elf is now a matter for the church. I will return with him to Dolthgurdar where he will be beaten and restored and beaten again until the truth is known. Then with no more secrets to reveal, the process will continue until Loth is pleased and satisfied that he has completed his penance. Of course no penance will ever suffice... Yes that is what will happen. it is a good plan. I will leave tomorrow, and I am bringing Zalsh's guard with me. They are in need of a new lieutenant and I will chose one for them. Still she did not seem to be speaking to anyone in particular, Almost as if there were no one in the room worthy of the announcement

The steward stepped in to the conversation, probably sparing Nal's life in the process.

'Wait a minute Honored Priestess. The disposition of this elf is a matter of security, and I am in charge of all internal security here in Nerr’tenden.'

The priestess seemed completely unimpressed.

'Did I not just make my need for a male opinion clear? No steward, I will hang him by the well a few days, then I will take him. He is in the hands of the church now. You will not interfere.'

The steward knew enough to hold his tongue, but Zacxh somehow knew the conversation was far from over. Something outside Zacxh’s purview gave the steward pause in letting her go. For the life of him, Zacxh could not fathom what it could be. Perhaps some problem with a priestess selecting a Lieutenant for Xulleyl. Perhaps that is where Ardul had come from.

The next few hours proceeded predictably. The Spiderguard escorted Flick back to Nerr’tenden and disbanded for a few hours. Nal and Valron consulted in the barracks. Xulleyl prepared for a convoy to Dolthgurdar, and questioned Flick. Zacxh stole away for a much needed bath and a stockade was erected near the well. Things were heating up.

Tension mounted. Valron was clearly upset by the undeserved fate of the non priest and the Steward was upset by the renegade actions of his Priestess. Trynn was exited by the concept of a new training partner and Nal was concerned for his own wellbeing with respect of his actions toward the daughter of Loth. Sorn was unhappy to have to constantly trudge back and forth to and from the dingy mineshaft. and complained about it to anyone who would listen. Only Inarra and Zacxh were unconcerned. Inarra due to her unaffected perhaps flippant nature and Zacxh because he saw the type of tension mounting that might lead to an opportunity for him to purge a cancer form the Underdark. He saw the death of a priestess in the very near future.

All of Nerr’tenden knew that harsh discipline and cruelty at the hands of the church were necessary to maintain order amongst Loth's dark elves. Zacxh knew there had to be a limit; a line between discipline and insanity. Dinlin had clearly stepped over, and Zacxh foresaw a rapidly approaching reckoning. More blood upon the alter of the spider queen.

The thought filled him with hope. The bounds of Spiderguard were loosening and soon he would be free to begin his quest of political and religious reform... A reform that with luck would soon find Dinlin twitching on the end of Zacxh's blade.

ChapterOne

Zacxh wasted no time leaving the arena. He knew the twisting hallways which wound out of house Ossund, but since his childhood eighty some years hence he had never followed them all the way through the door.. Zacxh reread his note. He was instructed to leave and meet a caravan but getting to the crystal gate would be no easy task. He was a secret slave of house Ossund not meant to be wandering the halls, and worse yet, he was presumed dead. Perhaps, he thought, he should try to escape via the service exit near the kitchen. He was unarmed and wearing only his soft boots and a bloodstained loincloth.

Zacxh clung to seldom used corridors with his torn ears tuned to every possible source of danger. Several times he had to dive into a side chamber or hide in a tight corner to avoid discovery. By the time he reached the kitchens he was nearly shaking with tension.

A few servants were working to prepare the middle meal for some house guards. They did not notice as Zacxh stole quietly into their presence. Zacxh crammed his body into a tight space between a scalding hot oven and a prep table. The oven toasted his flesh slightly as he waited and watched the comings and goings of the kitchen staff. He could not be discovered, so waited until there was a break between servings.

When only one Servant remained and was immersed in the task of washing pots, Zacxh made his escape. He grabbed a sturdy looking kitchen knife, and slipped out the delivery door.

Zacxh stopped outside the kitchen long enough to dig through a trash bin. He dug out an old filthy cloak and a tired leather belt into which he tucked his fine carving knife. The cloak had a hood and though ill fitting of his pit fighter's war shaped frame, it concealed his scarred and tattooed skin. He had little trouble, thus adorned, blending into the traffic leading out the crystal gate.

True to the prediction of the mysterious scroll, there was a caravan in need of laborers making for Nerr'tenden. A stern and impatient looking caravan leader tapped her foot and rolled her eyes despairingly at Zacxh's approach.

As the caravan made preparations to leave, other wanderers also joined the group. One was a Striking elf wearing Fine black traveling cloths and a creepy black blade. The pommel was decorated with a set of clenched teeth which seemed to grip the blade. Another was a strong well groomed Fighter wearing the uniform of a house guard. He carried a large wicked looking trident. The fighter looked loose and comfortable and carried his weapon with a careless ease which bespoke a deadly familiarity with the weapon.

The caravan guards ignored the newcomers for the most part. As they made final preparations, Rath, the caravan's leader, addressed them curtly. She concisely told them that they were expected to pay for their own rations and carry their own weight, and that she was only allowing for their presence on the off chance they might prove useful as fodder in any unforeseen skirmishes which lay ahead.

Zacxh merely nodded his head at the instructions and tried to keep out of the way as the caravan finally moved out. The handsome well dressed traveler kept to himself for the most part and the fighter spoke a bit with the guards and toyed a bit with a bandoleer of small vials hanging across his chest. Zacxh stayed near a line of chained dueagar slaves who shuffled along bearing gear and cargo.

For the first few days the caravan moved along the Underdark with good speed and in relative safety. Rath made several stops at increasingly small outposts picking up supplies and making deliveries.

One town (?) was famous for tea and Rath allowed a night for the travelers to enjoy the ceremonies and have a good meal. Zacxh traded his only valuable possession, the fine kitchen knife to a sour faced cook for a poor pot of thin stew and a rusted and dull dagger with a greasy and worn scabbard. Still the weapon had a nice balance and after countless hours of rubbing and scraping cleaned up well enough to be serviceable.

Rath provided sparse rations to her crew as they continued generally north. Both of the other newcomers, the creepy eyed dandy and the guard seemed a bit put off by the cheap rations, but to Zacxh each meal was a feast. (Anita) made several friendly remarks to Zacxh and seemed generally friendly but the dark brooding elf kept mostly to himself. For his part, Zacxh lied that he was a servant performing a menial errand for his house and tried to avoid saying anything which might betray the fact that he was an escaped slave and a fugitive.

Eventually, the group happened upon a slaughtered caravan. Bodies of a dozen or so guards were strewn into a shallow uncovered grave. As (?) the scout pushed ahead to look for an ambush, Zacxh pillaged the dead for scraps of workable armor and weapons. He quickly strapped on a mismatched suit consisting of Leather greaves and gauntlets, a boiled leather jerkin and bloodied bracers. He found two decent long thin blades and strapped them, crossing, to his back. He also found a nice hand crossbow and set a short quiver of bolts on his left hip. He replaced the scabbard but kept his own dagger as it had finally come to a fine edge and was Zacxh's first real possession in the world. As an afterthought, Zacxh collected up a few coins and a small pouch to put them in ignoring the disgusted faces of his traveling companions. They were the first coins he had owned in eighty some years.

Zacxh emerged from the shallow pit armed, wealthy, and happy. For the first time in ages he felt free. He was elated, and most surprising, was eager for the fight ahead. He was armed, by choice this time, and if he were to fight, he enjoyed the prospect of a true victory, not one sullied by drugging, poor equipment, or other underhanded tampering.

Just as Zacxh was tightening the last straps of his armor, (scout) the scout returned with news of an ambush ahead. He led the guards down a side hallway and as Zacxh Valron and Nal made to follow, Rath quickly deputized them and admonished them to 'Stay out of the way and not do anything stupid.' Zacxh had seldom heard less needed advice.

(scout) led the way, pushing about fifty feet ahead. He poked his head around a turn in the naturally formed stone and seeing no threat stepped around. The sound of four crossbow strings heralded the arrival of well aimed bolts which jerked and slammed (scout's) body. A gout of greenish foam erupted from his mouth as he fell lifeless to the floor.

The guards seemed shocked and confused a moment, so Zacxh acted first. He remembered an old elf trick a fellow slave had taught him and brought a deepened darkness about the fallen scout then, taking advantage of the gloomy cover, Zacxh pulled (scout) back around the corner and out of the line of fire. More bolts fired blindly into the darkness clacked ineffectually on the stone around them.

Zacxh took a quick look at (scout) and realized he was beyond help. Green ooze dribbling from the jovial elf's lips spelled doom.

Zacxh emptied his mind and let himself slip into that 'hidden place' in his mind. He became a being beyond pain. His senses became detached and super acute, and he would be so attuned as to be able to drive his blade right into the most vital spots of his foes.

Zacxh charged... And, as he broke free of his globe of darkness, found himself surrounded by guards and the other caravan joiners. Only the slaves and a pair of attending guards had stayed behind.

The melee lasted only a moment. Zacxh and Valron quickly dispatched a pair of ambushers and the guards and (andrew) felled the other two, yet this was merely a delaying force. The chamber narrowed and led around another bend. Zacxh and the guards joined Rath and entered a large circular chamber. It seemed empty and anticlimactic.

One of the guards motioned to the south wall indicating the presence of some suspicious looking cracks. Zacxh, two guards and Rath went over to have a look and were suddenly caught in the thick sticky strands of a web. Crossbow bolts flew 'through' the northern wall, and with them came the realization that the wall was illusory, merely a trick of magic, perspective and the dim shadows of photo luminescent fungi.

Three figures were concealed by that wall. Two fired hand crossbows into the captive guards and one was preparing another incantation like the one which had created the webs.

Zacxh struggled in0vain to force his way free of his entanglement while watching Valron ram her trident lethally onto one of the crossbowman.

The mage finished his incantation and vanished from view at about the same moment Zacxh finally tore free of the webs and partially dodged a hastily aimed bolt. The tiny, likely poisoned missile managed to nick his side as it deflected off his boiled leather breastplate. Zacxh never noticed his slight wound, and drove the point of his rapier into the belly of the remaining crossbowman. The doomed elf scooped at his spilling guts and crumpled to the ground as all the color drained from his shocked face.

Nal called out "Valron come to me and we will block the escape. Let the others flush him out. All sound stopped and the party collectively held their breath listening for some sign of the illusive mage.

"Infernus arachnidious!" The mage popped back into view as a blindingly bright fan of flames leapt from his splayed fingers and into the guardsmen still trapped in the thick sticky strands of the web.

"FOOF!" The webs caught aflame and instantly went up in a smoky greasy explosion of heat. Rath dove free of the worst of the flames, but both the male guards streaked horribly as flesh dripped molten off of their faces and limbs. They died screaming and curling into blackened gory horrors.

Rath, Zacxh and Nal descended upon the murdering mage with the fury of a cave in. Blows came from all sides and it was only a moment before the mage was trussed and tied to a pole. Nal seemed to relish his cruel interrogation of the prisoner and Zach left him to the grisly work in order to search the cave.

Zacxh poked around the cave looking for whatever could have put these brigands into such a defensive posture. He found two large sacks in the corner and was struck momentarily speechless as he discovered they contained a huge fortune in Semi cut rubies. Some as large as a fist.

"Hey Rath, we have a situation here... " Zacxh wanted to be wealthy just as well as the next, but all but two of the guards were dead. The chest was large, and they were still a good days of travel from (destination). This cache of wealth meant pursuit and suspicion and untold danger. Even worse, Rath explained that the rubies were identifiably cut and marked with the symbol of the House Godendar ruby mines at Tleth'tyrr. These were trouble.

The diminished party of six warriors and the six slaves set out soon thereafter. They shortened the shackles of the Dueagar and loaded them with a gagged and bound mage as well as an unbelievable treasure in rubies. Zacxh persuaded Rath to lend him (scouts) enchanted cloak of concealment and used it to scout ahead of the vulnerable convoy for trouble.

As Rath feared, the deep dwarves could not resist the temptation of all those rubies. All but two, as well as one of Rath”s trusted guards died the following morning when the hopeless bastards tried to make their escape. The remaining two were assigned to carry the captive mage, discarded in the combat. The caravan which rolled to the gates of (new barracks) was merely a shadow of the one which departed (crystal gate city)

A guard and an officer greeted the ragged band as they approached the gate. The officer wore a 'spider pin'. Zacxh was relieved to be done with the poorly run caravan and never looked back as he walked straight up to the lieutenant and presented him with the stone token he received with his note. It was accepted silently. Valron and Nal walked up and each produced similar stones. They were taken.

The lieutenant seemed amused by the haggard looking caravan and after only a moment led the way into a heavily fortified keep.

The Lieutenant seemed ungrateful for the rubies which as a token of good faith, and to be rid of their inherent danger Rath at the advice of Zacxh Valron and Nal gifted to house Oussund. He said they would bring nothing but trouble as they were ransomed back to their rightful owners.

He sequestered the guard and Rath in a separate room, and made it fairly clear that they would not live to see another day. Zacxh Valron and Nal were brought to a small barracks chamber and locked in. Apparently they had found their new home. Nal bunked alone in one of the double bunk rooms, and Valron and Zacxh took a room together. It looked like there was room for eight in the squad bay, and it seemed to Zacxh that he could trust the former Oussund house guard to watch his back. At least they had shared the road together, and they shared a confidence in the secret of the rubies. He seemed a quiet but steady enough roommate.

The Lieutenant came in awhile later. He apprised the trio of travelers warily before speaking.

"Well it seems you were able to arrive in one piece which is more than can be said for the balance of your caravan... You should choose quarters and settle in the rest will arrive soon..."

With that, he tossed each of the three a large ruby in the rough.

"Let these be a reminder to you of your trials along the road and of the danger you faced in taking that treasure. You were right to give them up as they are a political hot potato and would surely have burnt you had you opted to fence them yourself.

The lieutenant left without further ado.

last edited 2005-11-16 22:15:48 by Cliff

ChapterSeven

An Unexpected Return

Zacxh spent the morning among miners. Not many drow would relish the solo trek required outside Nerr’tenden gates to travel to the mines, but Zacxh had made the trip many times and despite the dangers of the Underdark, he enjoyed the solitude of his journey.

Some of the miners remembered Zacxh from earlier encounters. He knew his reputation for destruction and violence preceded him and he traveled armed to the teeth. Despite all that, he treated them as equals and deferred to their expertise in every aspect of planning a mining operation. He had gold to spend, and he wielded it loosely buying high quality food and drink to munch upon during his endless meetings with the miners.

Zacxh's goal was to gain the confidence of these highly skilled workers and promote the most competent of them to foreman for his dig. A few days of social and technical discussions would give him an idea of who was right for the job. He wanted a loyal and proficient crew. Proficiency could be bought with gold, but loyalty would have to be bought with the currency of respect. Zacxh paid it gladly. In fact he found the hardworking and dedicated miners a refreshing change in company from his grumbling and ungrateful companions. Mining is hard honest work, and for that Zacxh loved miners.

The deeply scarred warrior finished a few more casual meetings and decided to head back to the barracks to see what new trouble the Spiderguard was into.

As he approached the gates, it seemed something was wrong. Eight of Lt Ardul's guard were manning the gates and they visibly stiffened as Zacxh approached. He did not know why the guard was doubled or why they should be bridling at his approach. What Zacxh did know was that he would find it exceedingly difficult to bypass the security checkpoint using force. He approached.

'A bit jumpy arent you boys? Are we expecting trouble?' Zacxh walked inside swords reach to show his total lack of concern about his wellbeing. The guards had their hands on weapons and some shifted uneasily.

Their leader spoke:

'Identify yourself!'

Ridiculous, Zacxh thought his face was nothing if not identifiable and this guard, Welcth, was his name, was known to Zacxh.

'You know who I am Weltch, now stand aside, I am on the Captain's business.'

Zacxh Crossed his arms stubbornly. With luck this Guard would get angry and loosen his tongue. Zacxh was still trying to figure out what had Ardul's guards out in force.

The corporal of the guard had different ideas. 'Lay down your weapons and get on your knees'

Zacxh Grinned wickedly and looked from side to side as if to size up his provokers, though in fact he had them well estimated already and was already calculating a set of opening moves. They would make for a tough but not impossible fight.

'You are not going anywhere in this outpost armed and we are going to take you directly to Captain Xulleyl.' The guard seemed steady in his resolve.

Zacxh countered. 'You are Ardul's troop. Bring your lieutenant if you will, but I do NOT take orders from you.'

One of the eight scurried off. Zacxh subtly chanced his attack strategy to reflect the absence.

Ardul arrived only moments later and scowled at the sight of Zacxh.

'I had hoped not to see your face again.' He began.

Zacxh was not in a mood for petty word games. 'Well at least there we are in agreement Lieutenant.'

Ardul was not amused.

'Get on your knees Zacxh and drop your weapons. We will go to Xulleyl together.'

Zacxh thought carefully through his chain of command and decided to take the action most likely to get him to Xulleyl. He laid down his weapons and presented his hands for binding.

Just as he had hoped, Ardul and a pair of guards led Zacxh to Xulleyl. As they walked, Zacxh couldn't help but feel that Ardul was not so sneaky and traitorous as he might at first appear. Sure he was petty and cruel and small, and sure he had harbored traitors (Juell) in his unit. It was also true that his cousin was implicated in the initial mine cave in. But perhaps those things were merely circumstantial. Zacxh would be interested to know Ardul better, though he thought that possibility was remote at best.

Ardul dutifully escorted Zacxh to Xulleyl who, much to Ardul's dismay, dismissed the Lieutenant quickly.

Captain Xulleyl explained to Zacxh that there had been an attempt to poison the well, and it was carried out by an agent impersonating Zacxh.

Zacxh reported his activities in the mine, then was given orders to rejoin the Spiderguard. He bowed out with little ceremony.

He opened the doors with his boot and stormed in enjoying Sorn's glare at his lack of protocol and Nal's displeasure at the sudden lack of oppressive silence. Trynn and Inarra were examining a corpse and Nal was looking coldly at a well beaten looking slave.

Zacxh boomed out. 'So, did I die well?'

The question went unanswered and Zacxh went mostly ignored. Apparently, the Spiderguard once again was blind to his dark humor. Perhaps as was so often the case only he could understand the irony. Zacxh exhaled, disappointed but hardly surprised, and pressed on. He wondered if his humor was really as droll as they all seemed to imply.

The Spiderguard barracks was in typical disarray. No one had thought to clear the dining table, and consequently it was festooned with half consumed loaves of bread and moldering cheeses. Bottles and corks and the varying detritus of a table whose contents nourish the body but not the spirit lay strewn about. The sorry meal had been picked at like a corpse is picked apart by rodents, that is without regard to anything but the physical need to feed.

Zacxh curled his lip then turned to the task of cleaning it all up. As he did, he took in the intrigues and discussions of the evening. They revolved around how to best respond to the foiled plot to poison the well.

Zacxh looked at the poisoned slave, then at the table. He regarded the rapidly stiffening corpse in the center of the room then regarded the slowly warming cheese. He looked at the feces near the dead elf woman with the shimmering skin then regarded his dirty hands and nails. He was repulsed.

Zacxh decided there and then to stop imbibing of this world like some savage beast and backed from the table to wash up in a nearby bowl. He then removed all his gear and scrubbed it furiously. He cleaned and sharpened and oiled as if tending to the implements of royalty, and in his mind, he was, for he tended to himself.

When all was said and done, Zacxh regarded his masterwork weapons. They had been specially made and balanced for him. He regarded his well kept armor, his blades, his bow. Then he regarded his scrubbed arms and hands. Weapons all. Nothing more, nothing less. He would only expose them as necessary to vanquish his foes and nourish his spirit. He would keep them pure. he would eat only the most uplifting meals and distain all else. He would master his bodies urges not let them master him.

At the edge of the table stood the last unopened bottle of good wine. he searched for a vessel and at last settled upon a tiny glass goblet.

He gathered his 'meal' and ritualistically cleaned the glass until it shone.

He lifted his draught in salute to himself and his rebirth as something pure and ritualistically tossed back the mediocre drink. It was good but not great. A bit fouled by the cork. It marked his last act of animal indulgence.

Zacxh regarded his comrades. they saw no change in him, but deep down something inside him changed. He closed his eyes and focused upon it.

Thirst was gone. Hunger, gone. Lust, gone. His animal connection to and hunger for this putrid world, gone.

Zacxh took one last look at the sad table and grinned. Then turned his attention back to the discussions of the evening.

At length, it was jointly decided to make the impression that the well was spoiled.

To that end, Captain Xulleyl suggested that he Spiderguard lead a caravan of supposed water gatherers out of Nerr’tenden. meanwhile Xulleyl would set up an ambush within the city. With luck, the caravan would convince Orllylyl or whoever the well prisoners were that Nerr’tenden was poisoned and that it was time to attack (and fall into the ambush within Nerr’tenden)

Valron and Nal devised and approved the plan with little input from the unit , a fact which suited Zacxh just fine. He was tired of political posturing and looked forward to his next mission. He needed practice with his blades and had a few new moves to try in actual combat. Valron and Trynn had recently lost their interest in sparring with him. Perhaps he would have to find some training partners outside the Guard...

Zacxh retired to his quarters feeling both empty of food and drink, and at the same time more pure somehow, He could hardly wait to void his bowls in the morning, Then he could begin to fully divest himself of the animal side of his being. He wondered how his new form of mental sustenance would affect his physical form. Would he dry up and become but a walking sinew? Would his strength leave him. Perhaps he would just fall over and die.

Soon he would know.

Morning came quickly for Zacxh. He had sat and crossed his legs and dropped into a deep trance. He relived in memory every action of the day. When he came to, he smiled, pleased with his actions. He felt as though he were on the road to something great. Almost as if destiny were calling. He cleaned himself meticulously, and put a keen edge along with a drop of oil on his blades. He shaved his face and head clean then adjoined to the common room. he was one of the first. The others joined soon enough and soon some ogres a few conscripts were unknowingly poisoned by Nal and the Spiderguard moved out the gates. Zacxh and Trynn took the lead. the scouted ahead along with Jane, Inarra's soul stone.

Half a days march outside Nerr’tenden, They encountered Fals or at least someone much like him. He had ??? pinned down and close to dealt with those damn shurikin. This time the Spiderguard, at least Trynn and .Zacxh attacked. Trynn got there first and Zacxh immediately behind. Fals knocked Trynn silly in an instant, and just as Zacxh was preparing to strike, Valron issued a command to stop fighting. Everyone, Fals included, obeyed and a truce was negotiated.

At length it was negotiated that the caravan would return to Nerr’tenden. Valron sealed the deal. and the Spiderguard returned victorious. the rues had worked and fals' presence in the corridors was good intel about who was behind the attacks on the well. On the return, the poisoned conscripts grew visibly ill. Zacxh was sure that fact did not go unnoticed by the attacking force. The attack would come soon, and Nerr’tenden was ready.

Zacxh found a concealed spot in the main courtyard to sit and wait. He expected the assault to open with massive flame and destruction and did not want to miss the show.

It had been more than a day since his last sip of sustenance, and he felt strong and vital. Pure.

Zacxh longed for the fight to come.

ChapterSix

ChapterSix

Zacxh's final Command

For prologue to this chapter see posts 446 to 487 at:

http://games.groups.yahoo.com/group/spiderguard/message/446

Zacxh could see from the look of shock and perhaps a touch of panic on his face that Valron had not picked up on the subtle message Zacxh was trying to send. Perhaps Zacxh's message had been too subtly hidden in double meaning. That was dangerous.

Zacxh took a breath and momentarily collected his thoughts. He thought he had a captive audience, and hoped to make enough of an impact with his next few words to at last consolidate the Spiderguard into an effective unit. Perhaps he would at last bring Kadyel into the fold and end the infighting. Perhaps he would finally relieve himself of a command he could not hope to hold. Perhaps he could finally stop looking over his shoulder.

Perhaps.

He hoped that in the next few moments he would not be bathing in blood.

The plan was risky and hinged on a lot of only loosely held assumptions.

Valron and Trynn were Zacxh's two biggest concerns. Valron because he had made such an unreasonable and domineering bid for command, and Trynn because he was utterly conflicted in his loyalties.

Ironically the uncertainty in their support was the very reason Zacxh could wait no longer. The clock had run out on his opportunity to deal with the only remaining obstacle to a functional Spiderguard.

Kadyel.

Wait any longer and Valron would usurp Zacxh's authority. Delay, and Trynn would forget his vow to follow this next and final command 'without question.'

Zacxh's brief pause to collect all those thoughts was interrupted, first by a misled Nal who incredulously asked if Zacxh was foolish enough to think he could kill all forty of the elves present, and then by Kadyel who may have caught an intuitive glimpse of what was to come.

Kadyel quickly and in her melodramatic way tossed yet more incitements of Zacxh's failing leadership and made a great show of renouncing her 'rightful' claim to lead the Spiderguard by smashing the phony golden pin she had only moments before thrown on the ground. This unconvincing, conciliatory drama was punctuated with a little tear on the Wizard's cheek.

Zacxh's face remained impassive as he laughed within his mental fortress. The Wizard's actions only confirmed that her pin was just another in a long string of parlor tricks designed to undermine Zacxh's flagging authority.

He decided to act swiftly and with as much impact as possible. With luck this would be his last deed as commander of the Spiderguard and he hoped to place Valron decisively in command.

Zacxh took a last breath to steel his resolve. All eyes were upon him, and the stage was set as well as he could hope. He began his gambit.

'Kadyel, you have proven time and again to be an obstacle to our evolution into effective unit!'

Zacxh put as much force into his words as his rage motivated body would allow. Still, he wondered if his passionless eyes would convey the severity of his words.

'This can continue no more! So, you will swear three oaths to the Spiderguard here and now. If you refuse or waver in any way Trynn and I are going to kill you where you stand.'

Zacxh risked a look to Trynn to gauge his level of support and was deeply concerned by the conflicted look the spineless monk suddenly wore. He resolved himself to continue on and hope Kadyel didn't call what was rapidly and unintentionally turning into either a bluff or a pitched solo battle.

'First!'

'Do you swear on pain of death to now and forevermore renounce any claim to command of the Spiderguard?'

Zacxh forced himself to remain deeply hidden within his mind. He could not allow any bit of his anxiety to bleed through to his body lest he self defeat any chance of success.

Kadyel blinked and looked taken aback. She was obviously caught off guard and a bit confused.

Zacxh immediately saw his error. He had asked the hardest oath first. He had forgotten a basic tenant of coercion, get them talking and agreeing before you slip in the whammy. Crap.

Kadyel blinked, incredulous.

'What? you want me to give up *any* claim to lead the Spiderguard'

Zacxh pressed on. Fully committed.

'Yes Kadyel. Swear it now or die.'

She paused only a moment, then committed suicide.

'I refuse.' She said.

The silence of the chamber was deafening. No one dared move or even breathe as the moment stretched. Disaster hung in the air like a specter and it seemed somehow a violation of the moment to so much as twitch.

Zacxh felt his heart beat once... twice... then roared into the attack.

The chamber exploded into activity. The next few moments were a blur of clumsily launched grapples and attacks as Zacxh was besieged on all sides by every one of the forty elves in the cavern who could get to him.

Inarra attacked his mind with some alien mental force, probably trying to steal his resolve. She failed.

Trynn enlarged to titanic proportions and attempted to restrain him... and failed.

Nal's thirty some minions attacked en masse swinging their short swords furiously all about the dodging leaping warrior. Their blades glanced off his iron skin and phantasmal barriers like pebbles off a stone wall. Collectively, they succeeded only in pissing Zacxh off.

Valron lashed out and missed.

Sorn sent dark eldritch energies which went unnoticed by Zacxh.

In short, he was opposed by every elf that could in any way intervene, but in Zacxh's highly attuned and furious state, they all failed to stop him. All but one.

Kadyel just stood and watched as Zacxh placed his sword to her throat. She apparently decided that she could not hope to oppose him and played her final mind game.

Zacxh indeed paused, if only for a fraction of a second while his resolve wavered. His warriors mind and pit fighting instinct had a firm hold on him. Yet still he hesitated.

There was nothing for it. Zacxh retreated into his mental fortress and flung open all the doors of his internal terror. His arms bunched, and he brutally rammed his huge blade home.

Kadyel erupted. She became a volcano of blood and staggered back fatally wounded.

Wounded but not dead. She gurgled up something spiteful as she wheeled back only to be knocked flat by Trynn's enlarged fists. Zacxh quickly concluded that Trynn was trying to protect her by taking her out with a stunning blow. Perhaps he thought Zacxh was careless enough to not ensure she was finished.
