First Blood

The PC's all meet one another and share a meal in their "guest" quarters in the Nerr'tenden stronghold. The following morning, they are brought to the arena, where they meet Captain Xulleyl for the first time. She speaks for a bit about the promise of each of them, and that assembled they will form a great weapon for the House.

She soon gets down to business and the group is put into a winner-takes-all combat; in the end it comes down to Zacxh and Kadyel in a slugfest which Zacxh wins. The Captain gives him a Spider Guard pin and pronounces him leader of the group.

Upon return, the group rests for the rest of the day and the evening. The following morning, Inarra confronts the group with a licentious display of a shallow cut spanning her entire back from hip to shoulder. She informs the group that she knows the perpetrator and implies that she will have a similar rendezvous with them some evening.

For a detailed narrative from Zacxh's perspective, look at ChapterTwo.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:10:36 by Steve

First House

The First House of the City is responsible for keeping order, protecting the city and managing the flow of trade.

House Godendar is the First House.

last edited 2005-09-20 20:22:40 by Steve

Gaullidurth

Gaullidurth is a major outpost of Dolthgurdar, owned by House Orlylyl. It mines sapphires, but its real power comes from its strategic location, controlling access to a number of outposts.

last edited 2005-09-20 23:00:47 by Steve

Geldiirn

Geldiirn'Olg Oussund is the Steward and Sword Master of Nerr'tenden. His skill with blades, loyalty and ambitions have earned him the rare honor of the House Oussund name.

As Steward, Geldiirn manages the daily affairs of Nerr’tenden with competence and charm. He is good at what he does; and the fact that he handles the headaches of administration is not lost on Dinlin. Out in the remote stronghold, she lets him manage with more of a free hand than most males have.

He relies on Xulleyl to coordinate guard activities to protect the hold, guard the caravans and keep watch over the slaves. She keeps the guard units on careful rotation, and it is her ambitions that have caused her to create the Spider Guard for her own uses.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:24:17 by Steve

Gestalt Rulings

Gestalt Core Classes fixed for life of character: Nov. 13, 2005

The core classes you choose at level 1 to form your new gestalt class are FIXED for the life of your character. You can always choose prestige classes you qualify for at any given level and replace the related core class with the prestige class.

Normal rules: the srd says that at each new level you 'choose two classes' and combine them. Theoretically you could be a fighter rogue at level 1, a thief psion at level 2, etc. This is not how we are going to use the gestalt rules.

Prestige Class replaces related core class for gestalts: Nov. 13, 2005

When you choose prestige class(es) for leveling, replace the RELATED core class with the prestige class. For example, a thief-cleric choosing the assassin prestige class would advance as a cleric-assassin, not as a thief-assassin. If there is doubt about which is the more related, consult the DM.

Spellcasting / Manifesting Levels don't exceed +1 / level: Nov. 13, 2005

If you are able to take a prestige class that allows you to advance "+1 level of existing spellcasting class" (or manifesting class, for psions), remember that bonuses DO NOT STACK with otherwise identical abilities. For example, if you are a psion-sorceror and take the Cerebremancer prestige class (which allows you to advance as a psion and as a spellcaster), you would have to pick whether you wish to be a psion-cerebremancer or a sorceror-cerebremancer and you would only gain 1 level of manifesting/spellcasting with each character level. You would not gain +2 levels in either one at a single character level. This is a known exploit.

Note that this makes a few prestige classes irrelevant (cerebremancer among them), but that's a side effect of the power and flexibility that gestalts have over standard characters.

last edited 2005-11-26 21:55:43 by Steve

Hash'tal

Hash is the rogue trainer at Nerr'tenden. She is an insightful teacher with a quiet voice, but don't let that fool you--she brooks no lapses of concentration. Her grace and agility are astounding, giving her movements a near-supernatural quality.

Her body was returned to Nerr'tenden during the siege.

last edited 2007-11-29 03:57:43 by Andrew

Homeward Bound

The PC's travel from Dolthgurdar to Nerr'tenden as part of caravans. They travel as several groups or individuals, not knowing that the others have been summoned the same way.

Along the way, various troubles manifest themselves, but there does appear to be a troubling event common to all three: a ruby caravan from the House Godendar mines at T'lethtyrr has been ambushed and its rubies captured.

Each caravan ends up meeting an uncertain or grim fate at the end of the arduous journey, and the players are each brought to their quarters in the stronghold by Lt. Ardul.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:13:24 by Steve

House Aleanana

[Aleanana.gif]

House Aleanana is the 20th house. They have suffered a serious blow with the sack of Karsolithuyl, but appear to still be operating extensive covert projects to raise their fortunes.

last edited 2007-11-28 19:22:44 by Andrew

House Baenep

[Baenep.gif]

House Baenep ('Blessed by the Underdark') is the Second House of Dolthgurdar. As House Godendar is the undisputed First House, there are none below Baenep that can think of taking its #2 council seat.

House Baenep has developed a reputation for itself over the millennia as a strong patron of elven culture, supporting artists and the largest Sorceror's Cadre in the region. They maintain an efficient and professional army nearly twice the size of Godendar's, and have promoted more priestesses through the ranks than any other family.

For'tenden, a strategic access post and source of rare silkworms, is their most precious outpost. Other possessions include Fraxoleth, a mussels farm, and other minor outposts bringing water and food moss to market. Their outposts are nearly all concentrated in the Southern Branch.

last edited 2006-03-29 21:16:44 by Steve

House Council

A House Council is the advisory council of senior family and sometimes membership of the House. The role of the Council is to advise the Matriarch when she wants advice.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:20:36 by Steve

House Godendar

[Godendar.gif]

House Godendar (the 'Dark Hearts') is the ancient First House of Dolthgurdar. As the preeminent house, they have significant responsibilities in the city and marketplace. As the keepers of the city, they take tax on all trade by all houses.

Godendar wields vast influence in the region; no house controls more resources or collects more tolls than Godendar. They are significant patrons of the arts, have a powerful stable of merchants, and only House Baenep has more soldiers, priestesses and sorcerors. Godendar's coffers are reputed to be worth more than the next eight richest houses combined.

In addition to its duties in Dolthgurdar, the House has several outlying possessions, including the distant carving-mushroom farms at Rhinn and the ruby mines at T'lethtyrr, an outpost very near to Nerr'tenden.

last edited 2006-03-29 21:00:48 by Steve

House Keniryn

[Keniryn.gif]

House Keniryn is the 23rd house. Their family has been decimated in recent skirmishes with other Houses and even some infighting.

Keniryn distinguishes itself from other Middle Houses in two principal ways: First, their Drum and Dance troupes are famous in Dolthgurdar concert halls. Second, they have fostered intense protective loyalty from their soldiers toward the noble family: Keniryn's family number only six, nearly the smallest family in any House. This makes them an attractive target for other Houses looking for a step up.

Keniryn claims Bhaerynden as its outpost, a profitable gold mine distant from Dolthgurdar and in between Nerr'tenden and T'lethtyrr.

last edited 2006-03-29 21:51:38 by Steve

House Kilani

[Kilani.gif]

House Kilani has fallen. Rulers of T'lindeth throughout living memory, they were recently deposed and destroyed by House Kilrahel.

last edited 2006-03-28 23:05:19 by Steve

House Kilep

[Kilep.gif]

House Kilep ('People of the Underdark') is the 47th House.

Kilep is a poor house, and its workers are focused on learning how to be efficient and capable tunnel runners, but the reality is that they are more often used as simple guards, shock troops and menial laborers by other houses.

Several months ago, they suffered a serious reputation setback when two caravans they were leading to House Oussund were lost en route, along with one of their few capable captains.

last edited 2006-03-29 22:13:21 by Steve

House Kilrahel

[Kilrahel.gif]

House Kilrahel (the 'People of the Gods') has recently won the title of 13th House. House Kilrahel has toppled and apparently eradicated the long-standing rulers of T'lindeth, House Kilani.

Kilrahel's power comes from their well-trained Cadre and their priestesses; both groups are specially integrated with the Kilrahel army. Kilrahel is viewed by its new hierarchy neighbors as a sort of dangerous nouveau-riche; while well-armed, their cultural accomplishments are on par with the Minor Houses - the 'Tunnel Rat' houses!

The crown jewel of the Kilrahel possessions is their newly-acquired property T'lindeth, a mushroom farm with the powerful position of being the first outpost on the Southern Branch. Kilrahel also has an ancestral carving-mushroom plantation Moht'lethtyrr located far to the north, above Maeralyn.

last edited 2006-03-29 21:35:31 by Steve

House Melemtor

[Melemtor.gif]

House Melemtor ('Mothers of the Abyss') is the 36th House.

Melemtor is a minor House that specializes in caravan transport for other Houses, and is known for its professionalism and efficiency.

The tiniest house of all Dolthgurdar, Melemtor is currently suffering under terrible leadership from its Matron; it is unclear is she is going senile or even insane. A coup from inside or outside must be imminent; the House cannot continue as it is.

last edited 2006-03-29 22:14:14 by Steve

House Noquiryn

[Noquiryn.gif]

House Noquiryn ('Sacred to History') is the 14th house.

Noquiryn is a typical middle-powered house; they don't have the same across-the-board strengths and cultural achievements of Council Houses, as much of their wealth is dedicated to training what Sorcerors and Priestesses they have.

Their strategically located outposts, Cloibbrath and Erlynden catch toll traffic from every outpost on the outer West Branch. These outposts are the key to Noquiryn power.

last edited 2006-03-29 21:42:04 by Steve

House Noqusek

[Noqusek.gif]

House Noqusek ('Sacred to Adamantite') is the Seventh House of Dolthgurdar, holding a seat on the City Council.

Noqusek is renowned for their respect for the arts, particularly the performance arts, including music and dance. The House is also very pragmatic: they are well-defended by their soldiers, and have a powerful Cadre and clergy.

They own three outposts, two of significance: Llurth Dreier, a fresh mussel plantation and Dallnothax, a well-protected silver mine. These two outposts are only a few hours apart with no other outposts between them, providing significant assistance in times of trouble and also saving some toll fees on their mussels. Their third outpost is a small lumber farm.

last edited 2006-03-29 21:27:10 by Steve

House Orlylyl

[Orlylyl.gif]

House Orlylyl ('Guild of the Blade') is the 27th House. They are the only competitor for House Oussund in the sapphire trade.

Orlylyl's desperate and unlikely bid to gain control of Gaullidurth several decades ago has paid off handsomely; they are now a well-respected Middle House. After its war, Orlylyl chose to focus on fewer, highly-trained forces rather than large mediocre ones. Their soldiers are renowned fighters, and Orlylyl's name has popped up more than once in rumor as the likely hand behind some well-executed operations.

One of the handful of most valuable outposts, Gaullidurth is the Northern Branch gateway after Dusklyngh, and the sapphire mine there is the only one in competition with House Oussund's Nerr'tenden.

Valron has been revealed as an Orlylyl noble.

Increasing evidence supports the idea that Orlylyl was behind the incursion to Nerr'tenden's mines and that they have been disrupting caravans through the Catacombs, although the fact that Oussund caravans were the only ones untouched seems confusing.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:08:28 by Steve

House Oussund

[Oussund.gif]

House Oussund ('Heirs to the Spider's Kiss') is the 28th House.

House Oussund is one of a handful of lower Middle Houses that are in good position to further themselves in the coming years. Oussund has a thriving commitment to training Sorcerors and Priestesses, and maintains a healthy military presence. Oussund has several notable artists in Dolthgurdar, including the dancer Tal'nalthereen Oussund.

The very remote sapphire mining outpost called Nerr'tenden is the family's source of income.

The House's current rivals include House Orlylyl, which is the only competitor in the sapphire market, and House Keniryn, which controls a gold mine and armed checkpoint only a half-day of travel from Nerr'tenden. House Oussund caravans must pass through the gold mine checkpoint to reach the market at Dolthgurdar, and tolls are expensive.

Illiam

Understandably paranoid as a member of the small House Keniryn family, he is known for the small fortune represented by his personal armor and ornaments as well as for his skill as a dancer.

Steward Illiam Kenyrin was mysteriously killed while escorting a caravan of Bhaerynden gold to Dolthgurdar under the protection of his outpost's most elite warriors as well as that of the Spider Guard during an ambush by bandits who had been harrying caravans in the catacombs between Bhaerynden and Llurth Dreier. His body was conducted by the Spider Guard the rest of the journey through the catacombs as none of the Kenyrin contingent survived the ambush.

Taken to Dolthgurdar by Kenyrin forces, Illiam was ressurected by his family and has now resumed his duties in Bhaerynden.

It has been rumored that Illiam has some secret liaison with Captain Xulleyl of Nerr'tenden.

Kadyel

Starring Blake Tucker as Kadyel Stormbrewer

[kadyel.png]

She died for what she believed. For that she is blessed.

Kadyel Stormbrewer came from a family surrounded with suspicions and doubts about their lives. Dark elves live a secret and unknown existence for the most part, full of plotting, scheming, and self-interest. Her family taught her as a youngster that there might be more. Childhood stories of a fantasy world often enthralled her---stories where people worked together under a common goal without killing each other when disagreements inevitably flowered. Perhaps it was the strange powers her family had that made her such a daydreamer as a child; no one spoke about them of course, and they skipped a generation anyway so were easy to overlook. But her grandmother had a way with things---she had an unnatural ability to start cookfires, tend to the sick, and her soups could never be replicated even when she wrote down every ingredient and her students followed her every instruction. But when Kadyel came of age, she was able to improve her grandmother's recipes. No one pointed it out, but when the women gathered to eat together, the rapidity of the soup's disappearance was proof enough. This contented Kadyel for a time, until outsiders noticed her talents and adolescence arrived. Then she was exposed to society's suspicions and doubts firsthand.

Kadyel's teenage years were fraught with conflict, self-hatred and sublimation. She attempted to compensate for her difference by becoming a stout warrior amongst her fellow girls. Dark elves are indeed matriarchal, and Kadyel was determined to be the best warrior of her age so that no criticism could befall her. And she did well. A few were stronger than her, but none more agile. However, it was her strategic mind and strong sense of personal command that served her best. Always she was able to steer whatever group she commanded, made moreso by her newfound talent of blending in. With no powers or magic, she at last had found a skill that she was good at, one that was not grown from battle. She was a chameleon. She learned to listen and learn before she spoke, and had a gift for making herself seem like a peer to others. Once she realized she could learn and grow on her own, she began to apply herself more and believe in herself. She made peace with her ancestry, and began to understand how to use her congenital magic to her advantage. She found incredible strength in her newfound blend of prowess, magic, strategy and skill.

Finding her niche in the structure of society, Kadyel created for herself a life of promise as both a guard and a sorceror. It was not without suspicion however. Very few elves were allowed to practice magic. Her family was viewed as barely tolerable, for their strange powers did not conform to the codes of the drow. But never had they betrayed their house, and always did they aid the cause, so they were left alone. And Kadyel was allowed to live her life, hoping that someday those childhood dreams of cooperation and peace would arrive, despite her often violent duties as a soldier.

On the morning of her invitation to the Spiderguard, her grandmother had spoken to her. She said she would tell Kadyel more about their line, and where their destiny lay. But that conversation never occurred because of her abduction.

So what did Kadyel believe? She believed she was destined for something. Something different than a normal dark elf life. Something with a ending nearly unheard of. She longed for escape, for an existence that did not involve subterfuge and deceit. She longed to explore other places; to learn about the world outside the warrens of the drow. And she thought she had found that when she discovered her circumstances as member of the Spiderguard. Was this at last her chance to escape? Her chance to bury any doubts and fears about her powers by showing her strength as a leader? She suspected for many years that her family was something other---their very name made then stick out. What is a storm and how does one brew one? To nurture power within this society, power that could force it to change to fit her dreams or escape it once and for all required more than just being a soldier. Likewise, she knew no Matron would listen to her urgings for change or allow her escape if she was merely a member of the Spiderguard. She needed to be leader. She needed to be the public figure of such a group, the star of the cast for such a power to be obeyed.

"Do you surrender all claim to leadership of the Spiderguard, now and forever?" Zacxh had said. She had already surrendered her need to be leader for now. She had destroyed the Spiderguard pin and was ready to bury her need for the moment. But not forever. There was no returning to the life she led, that was clear. There was no more kindly grandmother to divulge her secret past, to clarify those childhood dreams she longed for. Her choice was to give her word and lose all her hopes forever, or to die now and show this bickering crew the value of honor, courage and conviction. To show them that she did not fit in here in this dark place. That she was something other.

For her there was no doubt, nor indeed a glimmer of hope. She knew how this society worked. She understood its need for blood and ascension. So when Zacxh spoke those last words, she accepted her fate gladly, on the point of that sword. She died for what she believed in: her dreams. For that she is blessed.

Email: <blake.tucker@stanfordalumni.org>
Website: [ http://www.blaketucker.com]
Photo Blog: [ http://blaketucker.blogspot.com]

Karsolithuyl

Karsolithuyl was until recently the seat of House Aleanana's power. Aleanana was pursuing several significant clandestine projects all of which were apparently disrupted coincidentally during the Spider Guard's visit to the outpost. During an audience with That Dude, Illithids raided Karsolithuyl and overcame its defense at every step. Surviving witnesses claimed that the Illithids were after information rather than simple feeding.

last edited 2007-11-28 18:37:32 by Andrew

Lolth's Fang/FightingStyle

The Fang seek to dominate their opponents through choke holds, pressure points, stun moves, and trips. Anything to keep a foe under control. While they aren't well suited to front-line combat, they make excellent assassins, bodyguards, and bounty hunters.

Dark elf monks usually prefer to deal non-lethal damage. The monk "culls" are always fought using non-lethal damage.

last edited 2005-11-01 21:07:47 by Nate

Lolth's Fang/MonkFeats

Dark elf monks value self-training and indepedence. They take special pride in developing their own unique fighting moves. Like wizards with custom spells, unique feats created by a monk are guarded closely, only passed on to trusted companions or apprentices. Even the rumour of having created a devastating new move can bring much prestige to a monk.

It is said that the monk who developed the "Blinding Fist" special strike had it given to him as a gift from Lolth for some wicked service he completed for her ...

There are rumors of particularly devastating feats with effects so wondrous they can only be supernaturally inspired. Only the most powerful monks and those who hire them know if the rumours are true. One such legendary move is often referred to as "I'll knock you into the middle of next week". Apparently, it can actually knock you into the middle of next week.

last edited 2005-10-26 17:28:07 by Nate

Lolth's Fang/code

1. Be strong

2. Cull the weak

last edited 2005-11-01 21:03:05 by Nate

Lolth's Fang/cull

The Fang have a particularly ruthless tradition called the "cull". If you are crippled, elderly, or otherwise too weak to continue advancing in your skills, a monk will challenge you to a duel. The duel is a farce of course, since you are obviously too weak to fight effectively. The shame of being culled is great, and this keeps the monks always training rigorously to avoid such a fate.

The culls are always fought with non-lethal damage for a knockout. The culled monk is now an outcast to the monks. She will never find another trainer to further her skills, and the Fang will disown her. She is dead to them.

While this is a decentralized, ad-hoc enforcement mechanism ripe for abuse, it is rarely abused because the only thing more shameful than being culled is to be beaten by the one you are attempting to cull. If this happens the loser usually accepts total banishment. Some monks with failed culls have gone to the surface the shame is so great. So it is a self-enforcing tradition and works well.

Culls generally only occur between monks of the same skill level as it is considered shameful to cull someone with obviously less experience than you. Although disguise *is* a typical monk skill, and dark elves *are* devious. Also, goading your enemy into culling you by feigning weakness would not be unheard of...

last edited 2005-11-03 00:06:52 by Nate

Lolth's Fang/reason

The monks are often employed by the clerics as bodyguards, bounty hunters, and assassins.

This is so well-known that it is rumoured that the monks are a secret army for the clerics, or even Lolth herself. Because of this they are often referred to "Lolth's Fang" or simply "the Fang".

Some even fear that the monks may be the unwitting tools of a powerful outsider preparing an army for a sinister revolution. The monks scoff at this but sometimes even they begin to wonder where some of the darker knowledge in their special moves has come from.

The clerics are too arrogant and self-satisfied to fear anyone, much less a bunch of obsessive meat pounders like the monks, so they use the monks as tools, like they do everyone else. The Fang have no special loyalty to each other and as often as not they find themselves enemies in the employ of two different House clerics.

last edited 2005-11-01 18:29:28 by Nate

Lolth's Fang

The dark elf monk tradition is unique and sinister. Their philosophy emphasizes personal discipline of mind and body. In fact, they have a Nietzschean super-man view of themselves and are even sometimes arrogant and disdainful towards non-monks, seen as weak and undisciplined.

There is no official order, they have no monasteries, they have no leadership or hierarchy.

Their philosophy of mind/body discipline is reflected in their unique fighting style, and their dedication to personal advancement is embodied by their practice of culling weak members who are not capable of advancement.

There is a reason they are called Lolth's Fang.

They take special pride in developing their own unique monk feats.

They have an unofficial code.

last edited 2005-10-26 17:27:39 by Nate

Lolth

Lolth is the deity of the Dark Elves - the Spider Queen.

Matriarch

The female leader of a house is the Matriarch. She holds life-and-death authority over all members of the household.

The Matriarchs of the top eight houses form the City Council.

Mindwitness

This nightmare of eyes and lashing tentacles flies across the ground without apparent support.

A mindwitness is a 6-foot-diameter orb dominated by a central eye and a small, lampreylike maw. Ten smaller eyes on stalks sprout from the top of the orb, as do four waving tentacles.

It is rumored to originally be the magical cross of a Beholder and Illithid.

Myyrix

Appearance

Of average height for a male, though more squarely built than the average Drow, Myyrix wears a chain shirt, well-worn leather breeches and shirt, and carries a matched set of long- and short-swords. He bears the scars expected from one working amongst the house guard.

His manner seems almost distracted at times and given to tangential comments, though few believe him absent minded after working with him for even a short time.

NPCs/TurNPC

Tur is... was... a female tunnelrunner in charge of the caravan that brought Trynn to Nerr'Tenden

Cruelly murdered by Xulleyl's men at the gates of Nerr'Tenden along with her slaves and retainers, presumably to ensure secrecy.

Two of her retainers, Hurm and Drak, were small-time toughs who attempted to mug Trynn not once but twice during the trip. Trynn managed to talk his way out of it once but was finally forced into using violence to dissuade them. Acting quickly, knowing he was flanked and outnumbered, Trynn dispatched Drak down a deep hole before dealing with Hurm by knocking him unconscious.

When Tur confronted them and discovered Hurm's plan to mug and/or eliminate Trynn, she threatened to leave him alone in the underdark unarmed, but relented.

Later, when the caravan was slaughtered, Trynn noticed Hurm lying dead, his final act an attempt to shield Tur's body from the assassins' arrows.

Nerr'tenden

Nerr’tenden is a relatively isolated roughside stronghold about 100 miles (a week of hard travel) from the city of Dolthgurdar, where House Oussund is headquartered. (See the regional map.) The stronghold protects a small spring of clear water (which happens to be secretly collocated with one of the two known sources of Hirthal) and serves as a base of operations for mining gems, specifically sapphires. Nerr'tenden is one of more than 50 mining or farming outposts that all support the marketplace at Dolthgurdar.

There are roughly 70 dark elves in residence at Nerr’tenden at any one time, and 80-100 slaves. Approximately 60-80 of the slaves are mining laborers and haulers; their numbers vary with mortality rates and on the speed of replenishments from Dolthgurdar. The laborers are mostly duergar, with a handful of orogs in the mix. The remainder are expert miners, duergar slaves who plan and direct the efforts of the laborers. The remaining 20 slaves at Nerr’tenden are split evenly between gemcutters and household servant-slaves; the gemcutters are svirfneblin and a duergar; the household servants are dark elves who are indentured or slaves.

The inhabitants of Nerr’tenden are a mix of blacksmiths, fletchers, cooks, guards and the like.

life at Nerr'tenden

last edited 2007-03-19 22:01:56 by Andrew

Nzerit'man

Nzerit'man translates literally to Nzerit[in search of]'man[weakness].

It is generally manifested as a house-sponsored 'cleansing' of elements within the house that are considered or evaluated in the eyes of the Nzerman [Seeker of weakness] to be weak and unworthy of support by the house. A 'cleansing' generally results in death.

Rath

Female Tunnelrunner of House Kilep. Hard nosed leader and pragmatic, chose to trust the PCs when she needed to. Was the only survivor of the escort party for Valron, Zacxh, and Nal.

Presumed executed by Lt. Ardul or his agent upon her arrival in Nerr'tenden to contain information about the Spider Guard, she was actually employed by Captain Xulleyl as a scout and operative.

last edited 2006-07-11 18:11:03 by Andrew

Rauvdril

The name Rauvdril means little to most dark elves. They believe that he is nothing but a character in imp's tales, a pretender to Lolth's greatness, exposed for a fraud and destroyed ages ago.

Now that Valron has revealed himself to be a priest of Rauvdril, the party is learning a bit more about the god.

Rauvdril is indeed a god, although one not often worshiped by dark elves. His domains of influence include Earth, Strength and Travel.

There are Ten Virtues that his followers must live by - to follow these codes is to live morally, to fail at any of them is to be weak.

Rauvdril’s Ten Virtues

Courage – be brave, be strong, do not show fear

Prowess – be excellent, be admired, be skilled, especially on the battlefield

Exploration – find new paths, new places, new things

Self-Reliance – don’t expect others to do your work for you

Discipline – stay the course, show inner strength, focus on the goal

Self-Improvement – always strengthen yourself to strengthen Rauvdril

Exert your Will – shape your environment, don’t let it shape you

Force is a Last Resort – save your strength for the times it is truly needed

Act with Determination – when the time comes to act, be swift and strong

Inspire Loyalty – impress and draw others to you by living these virtues

T'lindeth

T'lindeth is one of the two major outposts adjacent to Dolthgurdar, and as such controls the flow of goods from the south-western outposts beyond to the Dolthgurdar marketplace. The traffic is not as great or as rich as that through Dusklyngh, but control of T'lindeth has nevertheless proved highly profitable for its new stewards House Kilrahel.

T'lindeth produces delicacy food items (they are the only producer of the succulent Jil'kin mushroom) in addition to being located strategically. Until they were eliminated by Kilrahel, T'lindeth was the historic center of House Kilani's power.

last edited 2006-02-22 19:21:44 by Steve

The Mineral

Nickname for mysterious destinations marked on maps recovered from (presumably) House Orlylyl operatives in the Nerr'tenden mines. The "Mineral" chambers were recently opened by the Zaxch and found to contain overwhelming magical auras and strange caustic liquid in ceramic flasks. At least one of the two uncovered chambers binds a large number of demons. Sorn summoned The Demon with the name that will never be remembered who said that his kin had been sealed there by Illithids. It seems that the illithid incursions into the Dolthgurdar region may be intended to protect the integrity if not the secret of the chambers, and that House Aleanana may be pulling the strings of the conflicts in which the Spider Guard has become embroiled.

Trynn'lousha

Trynn is large and strong for a dark elf. He keeps to himself and stares too long when making eye contact.

He moves gracefully, like a trained dancer. He wears no armor, and carries a whip, a flail, and a net. Dark elves easily recognize these as the favorite weapons of the dark elf monk tradition, known commonly as Lolth's Fang.

Trynn's back and arms and legs show many scars, clearly inflicted by scourge and whip. These are the sure marks of a cleric's slave.

TrynnBlog/TrynnBlog1

First Entry

Dear Diary. I woke up dead today. I'm outraged! My head hurts, too. Damn, I should have been a cleric.

I need my mother.

last edited 2005-11-12 01:02:24 by Nate

TrynnBlog/TrynnBlog2

Dear Diary,

A lot has happened to me since my miserable failure on my first assignment as a bodyguard for the house clerics.

My only hope is that even Shaille's death was part of the ruse but I fear that Xulleyl is far too ruthless to risk leaving her alive. Shaille is dead, it is my fault, and the Oussund priestesses will have my mother tortured to death for certain if it is ever discovered that I yet live. In fact, my failure alone may be enough that they are punishing her anyway, even as I write this. It is a daily struggle to stay put and not attempt an escape in order to return to Dolthurgar.

Since the attack and my fake death I have been sequestered to Nerr'Tenden as part of some mad plot orchestrated by this Xulleyl who claims to be a Captain of the Guard for House Oussund. I have my doubts about that.

Upon my arrival she ruthlessly exterminated the cargo caravan that brought me. I am certain this was done more for my benefit than for any value to be had in eliminating the caravan. She was sending a message, trying to establish fear and dominance before even meeting me.

Well it worked. The callous massacre chilled me to the bone and I have no desire to cross Xulleyl. I doubt I would survive the day if I even brought her an instant of displeasure. This is the only reason I do not attempt escape. I owe it to mother to be wise and survive so that I can still save her in the future. If I were to be caught in mid-escape it would be my death.

Only the future can tell where this will all lead.

Signing off, By Lolth's Webs

Trynn

last edited 2005-12-22 00:08:31 by Nate

TrynnBlog/TrynnBlog3

Dear Diary,

Xulleyl calls us her "Spider Guard" and her first command was that we all turn on each other for her amusement. She called it a "test" but what did it test other than martial skill? I found this "test" to be a mark against her competence to be honest, because martial skill is no testament to leadership and other skills may be powerful and even overwhelming but they do not shine in the kind of free-for-all she orchestrated. Given time, some of those who fell first may become the most powerful of the Spider Guard. I found her game offensive.

Now I will describe my companions, as I suspect my fate is tied to them for some time to come.

After witnessing the brutal massacre of the caravan that brought me to Nerr'Tenden I was blindfolded and taken to a barracks where I was unceremoniously dumped off and left to meet for the first time my new companions. I was shaken and panicked and not at my best.

Valron immediately caught my attention. A large, imposing elf with a wicked-looking trident always by his side. He is an elf I would not dare to cross in battle, and he seems the type who is true to his companions above all. However, there is something sinister about him: he carries a number of vials and constantly sprinkles the contents in our food. I find this objectionable to say the least but I will not elaborate further, lest someone discover this diary. I'll just say this: he may be the one I'm looking out for but to be honest I hope he is not, as I believe Valron may be a loyal and forthright ally.

I just need to clear up this business with the vials.

Inarra is an imposing self-possessed beauty who clearly thinks the world is solely hers to manipulate. She may even be right but I hope she will contain herself. I can see that she could wield undue influence over me without me realizing it. Her presence and ... and breathtaking beauty are hard to ... resist. She's capable of anything. She's .... well, even the others realize the danger of letting her influence them so she may have the hardest time integrating into the group. It's so obvious she sees us as things to manipulate rather than as companions.

Zaxch is another who clearly displays loyalty to those he has chosen to be his companions. He and Valron are already inseparable, which I consider to be a point in Valron's favor. Like me, Zaxch was a slave but while he knows nothing of me I remember him clearly. Even then he was a formidable pit fighter admired by all the slaves, but after witnessing his prowess up close in the free-for-all I can only say that I hope to always be on his good side. He appears to be the most fit to direct our battlefield operations and I will gladly follow him into battle against any foe. One thing I must note. He stands no chance to remain as leader. The women are simply too ambitious to allow it. But he has already earned my loyalty as a companion in the Spider Guard.

Which brings me to Kadyel.

She is formidable and bossy. Yet she inspires confidence. I willingly offered her the leadership role during the free-for-all in exchange for helping me defeat the others. That was yet another failure on my part, as I couldn't even remain standing long enough for her to join me.

It is obvious that she is one of the most capable and self-sufficient of the group. I only fear that there will be some clash between her and Inarra or between her and Zaxch. Her ambition fills the room the moment she walks in and among this group, that may lead to problems. I only hope that others can see that she is the most suited to leadership.

Sorn displays the grace and beauty of a lifelong dancer. His every move betrays a trained eloquence of movement that is compelling and delightful to see. He was not built for combat yet he possesses an alien, eldritch power I do not understand. During the free-for-all, he refrained from using that power, choosing to attempt less dangerous barehanded strikes instead. He clearly had no chance to win using this tactic yet he did it anyway. Thus, I believe he is also the kind who chooses loyalty over glory, which I admire. He seems to hold a healthy respect for the females in charge, which is wise and appropriate.

Nal. Nal. What kind of elf is he? I don't know what to say of him at this point. We have exchanged few words yet that makes me the one he has spoken to the most. It is not because of him that I choose to sleep alone in the common room, but his intimidating and unsettling presence certainly doesn't make it a difficult choice. Sometimes when he looks at me, it feels like he is examining a bug in a jar. To call him "unsettling" may be a tremendous understatement.

I suspect he harbors a quiet and dangerous ambition that surpasses even Kadyel's naked desire for power. I have some hope that we can be allies but he is difficult to read at this point. I only pray to Lolth he never finds me helpless and unable to move ...

Len We is mystery to me. He is clearly trained in the ways of Lolth's Fang but there is more to him. He has revealed almost nothing about himself and he remains quiet and aloof.

Signing off for now, May Her Web Protect Me,

Trynn

Signing off, By Lolth's Sticky Web,

Trynn

last edited 2005-12-22 01:45:58 by Nate

TrynnBlog/TrynnBlog5

My parents were destroyed by House Oussund during a purge of traitors.

They tried to take us in our sleep, and but for a loyal friend who came to warn us of the coming violence, they would have succeeded. A quick, raspy scratch outside our residence. A scrape of stone upon stone. Two scrapes. Pause. Two scrapes more.

My father leaped to his feat in an instant, as if he had been waiting for that sound.

He trembled visibly, whether from adrenaline or fear I could not tell. But he whispered fiercely to my mother as quiet footsteps retreated from our door. "We are betrayed!"

Those words have haunted me ever since, and I am still to be convinced that he was really a traitor to House Oussund. He was betrayed. Why else would he say as much when there was no one of influence to hear it?

And there is one other piece of evidence in his favor. It is said that blood runs true, and the sins and virtues of the parents are passed on to the children. But if blood runs true then my parents were no traitors, for I am loyal to House Oussund.

That dark day of the purge, my parents were luckier than some others. They got a warning from a loyal friend at least.

I remember my father hissing desperately at us to "Go!" and then turning to face the intruders we could already hear approaching, his rapier held ready.

Unlike the clerics and nobles of the highborn, my parents held genuine affection for each other. I will never forget how they paused, how she squeezed his hand briefly before whisking me out and into the secret escape route they had planned. I've never seen a highborn so much as smile at a male but my mother stopped and burned precious seconds to squeeze his hand, knowing he was doomed.

We ran.

As we fled I could hear the sounds of battle, strange sounds to my young ears. The sounds of metal biting into flesh, of blood splattering a floor, the sounds of my father dying in his attempt to give us precious minutes for our escape.

...

We survived for weeks. First we hid outside of Dolthgurdar. My parents had secured hidden supplies for just this occasion. We moved each day, recovering food and water from secret caches out in rarely travelled tunnels. My mother spoke to me of House intrigues, of factions and of religion, of things like prestige and jealousy and power. I was too young to understand it all but I understood the lessons behind it. I learned that the House was not to be crossed. It was enough to even be mistaken for an enemy. House Oussand would find you and crush you.

Eventually we returned in secret to her cousin's house. The search was still on and she knew that she couldn't hide forever. She arranged a deal to give up in return for sparing me and they accepted. She was indentured for a hundred years and I was made a slave of the clerics. It was a marvelously successful outcome for us compared to what they had intended of course. All thanks to my father, who sacrificed himself to give us a brief moment to run.

I remember that she squeezed my hand as they took me away forever. She told me, "this is your new mother now," but I knew she didn't mean it. It could never be true. Even my loyalty to House Oussund could waver if she asked it. But she didn't ask it, and that is but more evidence to me that she was not a traitor. Since then I have seen her only a handful of times. Secret meetings arranged for short moments in time, a risk worth taking.

I was assigned as the personal slave of a young cleric. She took on the role of a mother, only very different from my own. Domineering, harsh and unforgiving. I was whipped when I did wrong, rewarded when I groveled. She taught me what I needed to learn. I am thankful to her for that.

....

I later learned they had executed my father, then revived his corpse to work as a mindless automaton scout in the territories threatened by psionic races. I do not blame the Matriarch for this. She acted on what information she had. It is only natural to crush your enemies while you still can, and to make future enemies think twice about the consequences they will face.

....

Over the years it became apparent I was gifted with unusual strength and agility, so my "mother" had me trained to dance for their ceremonies and gatherings.

I loved it. It was a release, an escape from my life as a slave. When I danced, I was free to move how I wanted, to be my own agent. Every waking moment of my day and night, every action every thought, were under complete control of my cleric "mother" except for when I danced. My dancing was very good. She rewarded me with lighter duties; I was not required to work the kitchens anymore. But she was still liberal with the lash when it was warranted.

It was arranged for me to be trained as a bodyguard, and so they sent me to an old retired guard with bad eyesight name Ghuan'Diirn, now living in peace near the outskirts of Dolthgurdar. The best part of my training was the long walks from the slave quarters to his residence. It was a kind of freedom, wandering the streets, witnessing the normal lives of Dolthgurdar. The clerics had no fear of me running away. They could find me with ease, and we all knew that my indentured mother would be punished for any of my failures. What they didn't know was that my loyalty to her transcended even my fear of them. I was able to arrange secret meetings with her more frequently. They were brief and innocent, usually just a quiet moment over tea while she asked me about my life with a mother's concern.

If the best part of my day was walking to meet with Ghuan, the hardest part of my day was walking home. The training left me beaten and exhausted. His training was brutal, but not cruel. He was demanding, but not vindictive. He may have been old, but he was certainly not weak.

My training was as much mental as physical. He trained me to endure, to suffer, to have a mental discipline that would serve me for any challenge.

We spent hours balancing with heavy weights, sparring upside down suspended from ropes, running courses blindfolded, fighting with hands numbed from ice, boxing barefoot on a floor strewn with sharp rocks, and more. Every day was a new pain. I lived with the pain. Every strike, every hold, every excercise was agony. I limped home every day. I resented much of it at the time, but it made me strong.

And he was able to spot my latency when no one else had. He taught me to look into myself, to dig deep from my own psychic will when I felt I had nothing left. I didn't quite understand what he meant but I tried. I could feel it tantalizingly near, a oneness of body and mind that would surely lend me strength.

He warned me not to tell the clerics of all we practiced. I found this odd, and scary, but I did as he instructed. As far as they were concerned, an old decrepit monk was teaching me some basics, that is all.

And then came the day that I died.

...

The priestess came into my quarters without knocking or even looking at me. At first, I thought for sure my life was forfeit, that they had determined some petty transgression and were sending me to the pits, which would have been death for me.

She was reading something in her hands and paused just long enough to snap at me. "You will accompany me as the Second. Now." And she left. She never even looked up. Her name was Shaille, but I only knew that because of overhearing conversations amongst the other slaves.

So, I was to be given my first assignment as a bodyguard to Lolth's chosen. Nearly an honor. Mostly just an opportunity to be punished for failure. That much I understood. I secured my weapons and met them out front, the cleric with her First. He eyed me with disdain and dislike. The bodyguards are constantly shifted around in rank and privilege, causing jealousy and intense competition. The clerics like it that way of course. They say it brings out the best.

"We are to meet at a rendezvous point where I will confer with someone. You of course shall remember nothing if asked. That is your role. Watch, protect, sacrifice." And she turned on her heel. The First walked in front, and I in back. She led us out of Dolthgurdar, into caves and tunnels.

I was jumpy and scared. I worried that my nerves would betray, and I focused on my inner will, as Ghuan had taught me.

They struck quickly and the cleric was down before I could even react. I saw the First draw his sword and then darkness descended as I fumbled with my whip. Damn! Then a loud cracking clap of sound nearly deafened me followed by a gurgling gasp from the First. I had no idea what to do. I turned to retreat and at least get out of the globe of darkness. That is when something struck my head and I was out, the smell of ozone the last thing I remembered.

...

I awoke slowly. Someone was dragging me along the floor, holding my armpits and pulling me from behind. Between my two feet, I could see three figures lying on the floor. The cleric, and the First, and another figure, all charred beyond recognition. Something odd..... something not quite right... the third figure was dressed and outfitted just like me! The same gear, and the same build, everything. A charred husk. Was I dead?

"He wakes". A figure crouched in my view, putting a small vial in my hand. "They will come to clean up. Stay quiet, they will not find you. Drink this when you are ready to move again." Then something heavy was slipped into my pocket. "Read this when you wake. Your masters will think you dead, so be wary". I drifted off, agony pulsing across my skull. My masters would think me dead, and so would Mother. I wished she could squeeze my hand one more time.

I finally woke again to the sounds of angry voices as they cleaned up the bodies and searched for clues. I had been stuffed into a crevasse down a side passage. I was cramped and hurt and thirsty, but alive. I waited in discomfort until they left.

I now make my way to the Crystal Gate, as the note instructed. What choice do I have? I have failed the clerics, my first assignment an utter failure that left a priestess dead. if they discover me alive they will be forced to assume I am a traitor.

And who is behind this latest turn for me? Or is it the clerics testing my loyalty? Or someone else entirely? My mother perhaps? I have no choice but to see where this goes. I can trust no one...

last edited 2006-01-19 00:23:10 by Nate

TrynnBlog/TrynnBlog6

I can only hope that my miserable display of ineptitude in the mines will go unpunished by Xulleyl. I pray she will give me another chance to show my worth.

We entered with confidence. We felt cocky I think, too cocky. It became immediately apparent that they were ready for us. They knew we were coming. Perhaps they were warned by some traitor among us in the barracks.

Nevertheless we started well. Despite my clumsy use of the innate darkness, we succeeded is pushing them back into the next turn of the cave. But that is where things went wrong. It was my fault yet again.

The mage blinded us all because I was too slow to realize the setup. I failed Xulleyl and I failed the Spiderguard. I should have understood that the mirror was setup for a blinding spell. Curse my slow wit. By Lolth's slimy tongue I will not let it happen again.

But fate saved us from my mistake in a way, although I am not convinced this newcomer is altogether a good thing for us. *Something* arrived and eliminated the remaining force, mage and all. There was nothing left. THE VERY WALLS HAD MELTED UNDER THE FIRES! It was the last straw. I wanted only to leave those mines and flee whatever demon was stalking us.

But Kadyel was right, we had to finish our mission. Kadeyl... ah Kadeyl. She seemed so well-suited to a role of leadership... at first. We'll see if she learns from her mistakes because even I can see she may lack the prudence to lead us in times of high stress and danger. Elves can die in the situations we find ourselves and and playing recklessly with our lives is not good leadership. But who else can lead us? It's strange to think of being led by a male. It must be Kadyel. Who else is truly suited?

Nal. Perhaps. He is not like any elf I have ever met, but his sheer force of personality cannot be ignored. Perhaps, even though he is male, he could very well act as a leader. I would have to be more convinced. I do respect his direct and forthright critiques. It feels honest rather than vindictive and I am fine with that. Afterall, I did make mistakes.

Inarra? No. Everything and everyone is a tool to her, even her own self! Yes, she is a tool to herself which is a bizarre concept I have just discovered. She is more suited to ... other roles.

Yet... no. Nevermind. Not Innarra.

Kadyel. I would like to think she will live up to her potential but only time will tell.

If I had failed a little less spectacularly myself I may have the courage to speak with her. Perhaps next time, if I don't fall on my face again in front of the others.

By Lolth's pointed tongue.

The Loyal Phoenix...

last edited 2006-01-19 00:49:30 by Nate

TrynnBlog/TrynnBlog7

The assassination

So, Xulleyl has turned us into assassins now.

When we joined up with the Keniryan contingent they already mistrusted us. So much so that we marched and camped separately at their command. We were to give a "gift" to Ilium. But of course it wasn't really a gift. I'm surprised the others took so long to realize.

At first they were suprised and a little confused after opening the box. But I knew what we had to do. It was obvious. I said as much and the plan took shape. Xulleyl had turned us into assassins.

But to what purpose? Why kill a man who is only going to be raised in a couple days? It's obviously some kind of message. But Xulleyl's machinations are opaque to me at this time. Apparently she felt it would accomplish something valuable and that is enough.

But it didn't turn out so well. I feel that once again we failed Xulleyl.

It started with a botched attempt at "delivery". In retrospect there's probably little we could have done. Keniryan was so paranoid and distrustful that no matter what they would have assumed it was us. Inarra was nearly killed and barely managed to get out of range of Selbs and Yaz.

At the beginning of combat I happened to be near the back with Kadyel. We heard troops approaching from behind down a narrow passage. We both decided to head them off, bottling them up. If they got through into the open who knows what they could have done. Zacxh yelled something to us as we headed down the passage but it wasn't clear. Something about "get back here". It wasn't until later that he made it *VERY* clear I had disobeyed direct orders. I pledged not to let that happen again.

Zacxh showed his disappointment by striking me across the face. The poor soul only knows the language of violence. I don't hold it against him. It bothers me to see him still so warped by his past, but hopefully he can grow past it.

Kadyel and I somehow managed to hold them all off. We took some injury but held strong. Finally they routed and as we returned to the main cavern, Keniyrin launched their attack on us. There was no room for negotiation. They wanted us dead and who can blame them? They were certain we had killed Ilium and of course they were right. I don't fault them their ferocity. They presented a formidable challenge even with Zacxh and Kadyel at the front line.

It was my inner mental power of expansion that got us the victory. I'm proud of that. Zacxh had a tattoo I'd given him. We both presented an impressive front. Some of the Keniryan minions simply fled from us in fear. But Yaz and Selbs may have prevailed alone. They were absolutely furious and better fighters than I've ever faced. Better than Zacxh even.

But the scariest moment for me came from our own side in the form of Nal. We were hard pressed, fighting ferociously, when suddenly Nal leaped between Zacxh and I and with a loud curse in an unintelligible language he lightly touched Yaz on the forehead, nothing more.

For a silent, eerie moment both stood still like two dancers frozen in time, and then Yaz slipped quietly to the ground. She was dead.

I nearly forgot to continue fighting Selbs as I stared at Nal in wonder and awe. Even Selbs was affected I believe because after that her fighting was lackluster, as if too shocked to really focus anymore. Nal melted back into the rearguard and was silent as we mopped up the remaining Keniryan resistance.

I will never forget that moment.

My Lolth's web protect us...

Trynn

last edited 2006-04-16 21:30:44 by Nate

Valron's Message

From Valron:

Respected Noble Mother,

As you must know, I have been employed for nearly 20 years as a guard in the service of House Oussund. Several months ago, my death was feigned while I was moved to a new, elite unit called the Spider Guard, and stationed in Nerr’tenden outpost.

Two days ago I met an intruder, an elf who recognized me and deferred to me as a noble of House Orlylyl. He was clearly a House Member who went by the name of Falt. Seeing him has brought my past into stark relief. Although I did not recognize him (and had to pretend to misunderstand him because of my companions), this elf can vouch for my identity.

Captain Xulleyl appears to be grooming our elite group for some kind of power play within House Oussund. You should know that your ‘expedition’ forces have been destroyed by the Spider Guard. Now that I have learned House Orlylyl is targeting Oussund aggressively, I cannot continue to let myself be used by her if it will mean that I must contest my own House.

I offer to act as an agent for House Orlylyl to aid in the operation to exploit House Oussund's mines. I bring the other extraordinary members of the small, elite Spider Guard with me, as they are eager to work for a House with great potential status.

I can arrange for the completion of the mission now as an insider, as other House Orlylyl efforts have failed.

Please let the Honored Matron know that she has a new weapon.

Your humble servant,

Valron’dar Orlylyl

ValronBio

One-hundred and forty-one years ago, Valrón’dar was born to a Cleric mother, Qualn’dril, and metal worker father, Tluth’ididyrr in the house of Orlylyl. Not being female, Valrón learned silver smithing from his father and watched younger sister, Lael’Thara train to be a cleric under his mother’s doting tutelage. Feeling the pressure to live up to her mother’s high standards, Lael deceptively uses Valrón to practice her skills. Lael swears Valrón to secrecy that he is helping her. After years of helping his sister study, Valrón becomes relatively skilled in the ways of a Cleric and grows resentful that he will never become a priest in his house. In finding an outlet for his pent up frustration, Valrón becomes an excellent fighter and is posted to the house Guard when he comes of age.

One day, Lael is given the robes of a full priestess, even though Valrón knows she could not have possibly passed her test. Valrón loses it, curses his mother and the Spider Goddess, and storms off in a rage. Valrón travels a short distance away from the city, and levitates up to his secret sanctuary. He centers himself, and for the first time prays for guidance, but not to Lolth.

A strange man suddenly appears before him, introducing himself as Nal’dax. Nal’dax tells Valrón that if he prays to Rauvdril then he will help him become a full Cleric. Nal’dax tells Valrón that there is a secret movement afoot to quell the powers of Lolth by bringing in Rauvdril. Nal’dax’s job is to seek out those with the potential to learn the ways of a Cleric and who also have the charisma and talent necessary to begin spreading his word without being found out and killed.

Nal’dax tells Valrón that he must train on his own under the guidance of Rauvdril and the domains of Strength and Travel. When he has become accomplished in the ways of Teleportation and Righteous Might (the 5th order) he will be visited again by Nal’dax to be taken to meet others like him in the Secret Society of Rauvdril. Nal’dax tells Valrón that just as he trains in fighting, he must also equally train himself in ways of the Cleric. But he must be cunning and not allow others to find out what he is doing.

Happy to finally have found some place in the world, Valrón sets off back to House Orlylyl only to find a war afoot between Orlylyl and Oussund. He learns that Oussund has attacked Orlylyl because Orlylyl owns the only other sapphire mine, Gaullidurth, which is better located than Oussund’s mine at Nerr’tenden. Valrón enters the fight on behalf of his House but is captured by Oussund. Oussund makes a ransom offer to Orlylyl for Valrón’s safe return but Orlylyl refuses to take Valrón back, telling Oussund to just kill him because of Valrón’s disrespect to his House and to Lolth.

Oussund instead decides to keep Valrón alive because of his exceptional talent as a fighter and future political value. If any other house decided to destroy Orlylyl, Oussund could present Valrón as evidence of a living nobility of Orlylyl. This would cause the victor house to be destroyed as well, thus taking out two houses at once.

Having been left for dead by his House, Valrón joins the Guard of House Oussund, where he begins his self training as fighter and closet cleric. Valrón expects that his house will eventually try to contact him, either to kill him or get him to act on their behalf as a spy in Oussund, or both. One fateful day Valrón eats poisoned porridge for breakfast and keels over.

last edited 2006-07-11 18:18:05 by Steve

Wicked Courtesan

Members of this prestige class are dancing, mincing, simpering, uh ... women of the night. What the world does not see however, is the need to charm her way into your heart, uh literally. She'll try to cajole, control, manipulate or dominate you, and should those 'delicate' tactics fail, mince about and put a poisoned arrow through your heart. Take that cupid!. No sneak attacks in the dark for her. When you die it will be looking into her eyes, confused and surprised that such a cute simpering litte thing would do this to you, and should the courtesan be good enough, maybe even glad that their radiant face was the last thing you saw.

Based loosely on the Scout class and the Assassin Prestige class http://d20srd.org/srd/prestigeClasses/assassin.htm, see Substitutions from Assassin Base below.

Hit Die

d6

Requirements

To qualify to become a wicked courtesan, a character must fulfill all the following criteria

Abilities

Charisma 16+

Skills

Diplomacy 8 Ranks, Intimidate 8 ranks, Perform 5 ranks

Special

The character must sleep with someone just for the purpose of manipulating and betraying them later.

Class Skills

Balance (Dex), Bluff (Cha), Climb (Str), Craft (Int), Decipher Script (Int), Diplomacy (Cha), Disguise (Cha), Escape Artist (Dex), Forgery (Int), Gather Information (Cha), Hide (Dex), Intimidate (Cha), Jump (Str), Listen (Wis), Move Silently (Dex), Open Lock (Dex), Perform (Cha), Search (Int), Sense Motive (Wis), Sleight of Hand (Dex), Spot (Wis), Swim (Str), Tumble (Dex), Use Magic Device (Cha), and Use Rope (Dex).

Skill Points at Each Level

8 + Int modifier.

Class Features

Weapon and Armor Proficiency

Charmers gain no additional proficiency in any weapon or armor.

Poison Use

Dark Courtesans are trained in the use of poison and never risk accidentally poisoning themselves when sliding a poisoned needle into someone's wrist, or swabbing contact poison across the back of a lovers neck (you get the point), oh yeah and putting it on blades too, etc.

Charm Touch

If an Dark Coutesan studies her mark for 3 rounds and then touches her "new friend" they must make a Will save with a DC of 10 + the Dark Coutesans Level + the Dark Coutesan Cha modifier or become charmed as per the Charm Person spell. this effect is not subject to spell resistence as it an aspect of the Dark Coutesans charismatic persona. The mark may be engaged in combat, and so may the Dark Coutesan. The Dark Coutesan may not have attacked the mark during the 3 rounds of study, and must make a DC18 concentration check each round to maintain her study if engaged in combat. If she is touching the mark during combat she must make a successful touch attack. Once the Dark Coutesan has completed her 3 rounds of study she must touch the mark within 3 rounds or must begin again. The DC of this power is affected by How Charming class ability.

Spells

Beginning at 1st level, an Dark Coutesan gains the ability to cast a number of arcane spells. To cast a spell, an Dark Coutesan must have an Charisma score of at least 10 + the spell’s level. Dark Coutesan bonus spells are based on Charisma, and saving throws against these spells have a DC of 10 + spell level + the Dark Coutesan's Charisma bonus. When the Dark Coutesan gets 0 spells per day of a given spell level she gains only the bonus spells ahe would be entitled to based on his Charisma score for that spell level.

The Dark Coutesan's spell list appears below. A Dark Coutesan casts spells just as a bard does.

Upon reaching 6th level, at every even-numbered level after that (8th and 10th), a Dark Coutesan can choose to learn a new spell in place of one she already knows. The new spell’s level must be the same as that of the spell being exchanged, and it must be at least two levels lower than the highest-level Dark Coutesan spell the Dark Coutesan can cast. A Dark Coutesan may swap only a single spell at any given level, and must choose whether or not to swap the spell at the same time that she gains new spells known for that level.

*Provided the Wicked Courtesan has sufficient Charisma to have a bonus spell of this level.

How Charming (Ex)

Beginning at 2nd level, the Dark Coutesan becomes so charming, it becomes harder to resist his enchantment/telepathy spells/powers. The save DC for any enchantment/telepathy spell/power increases +1. This rises to +2 at 5th level and +3 at 8th level. These increases are cumulative with those granted by the Spell Focus and Greater Spell Focus feats, or their psionic equivalents.

Mincing Feet

Fleet of foot and light on her feet, the Dark Coutesan gains a bonus of +10ft to her movement.

Distracting Presence

Due to their alluring nature and swaying charming aspect, Dark Coutesans gain their Charisma bonus to their AC. They retain this even when they would normally loose their Dexterity bonus (e.g. when flat footed). They loose this bonus if they are concealed from the attacker or behind cover. They also loose this bouns if they should wear armor heavier than light.

Unfettered Feet

The Dark Coutesan's movements are too much to be contained by mortal means. She can easily slip out of bonds, grasping patrons, grapples and confining spells. This ability is per the Freedom of Movement spell. She looses this ability if wearing medium or heavy armor or is encumbered.

Wicked Courtesan Spell List

Wicked Courtesans choose their spells from the following list:

1st Level

comprehend languages, disguise self, detect poison, feather fall, ghost sound, obscuring mist, silent image, true strike.

2nd Level

alter self, cat’s grace, eagle’s splendor, enthrall, knock, invisibility, silence, tongues, touch of idiocy.

3rd Level

clairaudience/clairvoyance, invisibility sphere, major image, haste, charm monster, glibness.

4th Level

discern lies, dimension door, greater invisibility, locate creature, lesser geas, neutralize poison, poison, shadow conjuration.

Wizard

There are some dark elf wizards, but dark elves seem to be naturally drawn to innate casting a la Sorceror. Being a wizard is tough for dark elves; their darksight doesn't allow them to read wizardly writing - they need to light candles to see, and nobody likes that. They also need to tote around scrolls, books, candles and flint. They're also 95% motivated by academic pursuits and research. They're not likely to go out adventuring. Besides, when it comes down to it, dark elves really are good at being sorcerors.

Yaz

Commander of House Kenyrin's elite guard at Bhaerynden and trusted bodyguard of Illiam. Imbued by her master with an intense distrust of outsiders as well as an equally fierce loyalty to him. Regarded the Spider Guard as inferiors and foes from the moment she met them. Yaz was slain along with her entire contingent during an ambush in the catacombs before she could testify as to the circumstances of her master's death.

ZacxhBio

“Crack!... Crack! Crack!”

Lucinda’s vicious snake headed whip bit again and again.

“Crack”

“You ungrateful little bastard! Don’t you even have the sense to cry out. You would deprive your mistress of the pleasure of your song!!! Well, I will see to it that you sing.”

“Crack!”

Zacxh knew his reactions or lack thereof would have little effect on the outcome of this beating. He had been whipped too many times before to be conned by the enraged words of a priestess. She would whip him until either he fell insensible or until she found something else to appease her cruelty. In Lucinda’s case it would probably be the former. She loved to see a male fall victim to her wrath.

“Crack, Crack, Crack…” “Scream you insolent bastard!!!”

A few years ago he might have even done it. He might have thought that by screaming he would appease her in some way. It would work on mistress Serinill, maybe on Mistress Theria too. But this Lucinda, well she was a real piece of work. His only defense would be his inevitable weakness.

Therein lay the problem. His weakness was beginning to fail him. His body had grown large and tough it is true, but that was not it. Larger more formidable males would have collapsed by now. Zacxh had found a ‘hiding spot’ in his mind. It was strange, and in a way he knew it had been there all along, but now he could run there and take shelter. He used to feel a great sense of despair and loss when his body was beaten and deformed, and it was just that attachment that had concealed the hiding spot from him. He now knew that his body was not related to his mind, but was simply its vehicle.

Today His vehicle was going to be beaten into a bloody rag.

“Crack” “Fall you insolent pig”

Zacxh could hear the Snake headed whip. He could, in a detached way, feel the painful neurotoxin of the vipers every bite. But the pain lived in his nerves and his brain. It no longer penetrated his mind. Unfortunately, that meant that his battered, branded, tattooed, and pierced frame would have to fend for itself. Loss of blood and shock would eventually bring it down, but it would take much longer. This was not pleasing to the Mistress.

Actually she had found other more satisfying subjects for her pleasure, and seemed almost apathetic and mechanical in her abuse these days.

“Crack!” “I will flay your flesh and feed it to the worgs you insolent pig, now cry out your devotion to me or DIE!!!”

Zacxh smiled instead. He found it sad and slightly amusing that she was so disinterested in his torture that she had called him ‘pig” again. She had definitely lost interest.

It wasn’t always this way. For a time, he had actually even been favored by the priestess of House Oussund. They had utterly destroyed his family in a raid thereby raising the status of their house. He was so young then. Barely even a boy. He had been born into the role of Guard-leader aspirant. Had his house survived, he would have an entire section under his command even now. He would have been killing priestesses in routine raids and watching *them* cry out for mercy. Ah well. His lot was not so bad.

He had recently come to appreciate his position. He was a pit fighter, and a champion of House Oussund. As such, great care was taken to ensure he was as prepared as possible for his next bout. As a child he had learned to pounce on other boys and orcs and lizard folk quickly and quietly. He knew just where to slide his knife to still a beating heart or disable a troublesome sword arm. He had killed off all his kin in the first year or so of his enslavement. He was strong cunning and quick in combat and thus proved to House Oussund his worth.

Like any prize they kept him in good repair, or at least fully functional. His missing digits were painfully and grudgingly replaced by chiding priestesses who beat him senseless with clubs and whips for the favor. His right ear was a tattered rag and his ebony skin was so stitched with grey scars that it was difficult in some areas to find any virgin flesh at all. His knuckles were thick and knobby from repeated breaking and his nose was flat and round like an orc’s. His tattoos and marks of ownership were all but indiscernible anymore, lost in the tattered menagerie of his flesh

Yes, She would beat him into a pulpy pile of goop. Then he would be salved and stitched up by some servant and left to his fevers and dementias. He would lie in a painful ball for days or weeks and would eventually come to his senses. Then a bout. Would it be a beast again? Maybe a young troll. He would be given a spear or sword, sometimes a net or sharpened stick. He would be cast into darkness or blindingly painful light and shoved into some cramped space to fight to the death. Then, as a reward for victory he would be forced to couple with some priestess or another who would chastise and goad him for his lack of enthusiasm then proceed to beat him again into a bleeding retching pile of goo. It was an endless cycle and would eventually end in death. Zacxh had grown accustomed to the cycle and had actually begun to look forward to his fights, but now he knew he was in danger. His lack of care for his body’s wellbeing was beginning to become apparent and so he no longer was of use to the priestesses of Loth. He would soon be sold to the mines or tortured to death or sacrificed in some way. He knew his end was near. The most likely form of his demise would be some skilled of overpowering adversary in the pit. His priestesses would drug or disable him in some way and bet heavily against his victory.

Perhaps today would be that day. He had heard whisperings that he was to be wrapped in leather armor and masked to disguise his wounds and sent into the pit against a renowned champion of another house. If true, He was doomed. His arms and legs were hanging limp and near lifeless. Even the dangerous venom of a green mobeus spider would barely stimulate him enough to walk. He would clutch his spear and drag himself about, but there would be no strength. Yes, at long last, this was probably going to be the day.

Zacxh had barely noticed, but the beating had stopped. Where had everyone gone? He pulled himself up and found that the door to the arena was not open. He would not fight today. Instead, the passage to the observing deck lay open. He was meant to watch a bout? He struggled with the idea a moment as he had never watched one before, but soon crept up the stairs to a private observation booth. No one would see him here and there was a not addressed to him on the seat.

Two combatants entered small private arena. All around were other observation booths shrouded in darkness. How many Dark Elves were watching. One of the combatants was a large and only slightly drugged ogre the other had the same build and stance as Zacxh. Both warriors were armed with small sharp pikes and maked to hide their faces. The elf was scarred and torn of body and watching him was like looking in a reflecting pool.

The combat was short. The Dark elf died on the ogre’s pike after only a single failed parry. Zacxh opened the note.

Zaxch

Zacxh'leborin of the fallen house Leborin...

is one of the most fierce looking Elves you will ever meet. He stands 5 feet tall and is dressed in rags. His strong tough body is covered in so much scar tissue that it is difficult to find any uncut flesh. The stubble on his bald head suggest that if it were allowed to grow, his hair would only poke through the managarie of ruined flesh in patches. Yet despite all this there is a handsome and confident air about the dark elf. Obviously a slave, there is a vacantly defiant cast to his purple eyes.

At games start he wears a hodge podge of salvaged and bloody leather armor bits and two mismatched rapiers all covered in a dark lizardskin cloak.

He never looks anyone in the eye. As a good slave should not...

Conspicuously absent is the "Spidergaurd Pin." As are the orders he might cast about due to its possession.
