Zilsh

Zilsh was the scout and assistant for Rath, who led a tunnel runner caravan for House Melemtor. He was friendly and cheerful with the PC's he met in the caravan (Nal, Zacxh and Valron).

He was slain while investigating the ambush of House Godendar's ruby caravan.

last edited 2005-11-26 23:06:59 by Steve

alignment

Alignment is typically used in the D&D game to give a starting point for characters, and deliver some help to players in determining their character's motivations, philosophy, beliefs, etc.

Darkelves do not neatly fit into single alignment slots - most of the time they act as 'Lawful Evil', but they will often plan and sometimes act as 'Chaotic Evil'. This is a reliable and consistent factor among all darkelves.

Darkelf morality and psyche have been outlined in the dark elf section of this wiki. Since all of the PC's and the majority of the NPC's have this same base morality, Alignment ceases to be of use for this campaign.

Instead, use the dark elf section and refer to the new rules on virtues and flaws for campaign rules to help generate interesting and varied darkelf characters.

Note that spells and items that use alignment are hereby eliminated; detect good/evil, alignment-based attacks, etc will not be used in this campaign.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:19:32 by Steve

ambition

Every Dark Elf has ambitions of one degree or another. Every individual and House wishes to increase its standing, its prestige and power over others. This is an undeniable and omnipresent fact about all Dark Elves.

last edited 2005-09-19 00:12:29 by Steve

artistic

Dark Elves admire things of beauty - objects, people, artistic creations, music, food and dance. In fact, no Dark Elf can reach adulthood without becoming proficient in at least one cultural art form. To fail to do this would be an insufferable humiliation to the House, and would leave the individual little better than a barbarian of a lesser race.

last edited 2005-09-19 00:12:42 by Steve

barbaric

The Dark Elves are as sophisticated, artistic and cosmopolitan a society and people as any other race on earth - the closest comparison would likely be that of the burn elves of the surface. They look down on barbarism as any other civilized people would - with disdain.

last edited 2005-09-19 00:13:49 by Steve

bath and spa

The bath is a standard comfort of darkelf society. Waters are heated or drawn from a natural hot spring, scented with herbs and used for soaking tired and tense darkelf muscles. Skilled bath masters prescribe herbal mixtures and compounds for particular maladies, provide massage and tend to guests in the bath house.

last edited 2005-09-24 03:23:22 by Steve

bath house

The bath house is a place very unlike most other parts of a darkelf community: it is lighted. Because the heat of steaming water can interfere with darksight (the steams can conceal the body heat of would-be assassins), bath houses are kept well-lighted for the safety of those inside.

last edited 2005-09-19 00:15:22 by Steve

bath master

Similar to tea masters, Bath Masters are experts in a critical social art - in this case, relaxation (instead of civility). A Bath Master and their staff are often trained as bodyguards in addition to their more expected tasks, as guests are more vulnerable in their care than at other times. They are also in charge of the bath house.

last edited 2005-09-19 00:16:13 by Steve

burn

The Burn is the Dark Elven name for the surface world, inhabited by humans, Burn Elves, and others under the harsh and incendiary presence of the Sun.

last edited 2005-09-19 00:16:31 by Steve

character background

It is important that your character have a background. The history and experiences of your character will inform the decisions you make during character creation and then during each and every session.

The PC's in this game have been brought together to form an elite group called the Spider Guard. You have come from a variety of backgrounds - some possible ones might be:

  • a noteworthy slave

  • a captured member of another family

  • a very junior daughter or son of the family of House Oussund

  • a talented guard, sorceror, etc.

  • anything else that fits in with the world as outlined in this wiki site.

Feel free to put in story and character hooks for Steve to use if you wish to have more emphasis on your character during the campaign.

Make sure that you specifically address some experience having to do with one or more of the personality / social factors described in the Roleplaying a dark elf PC section.

Your Character Background can be as short or as long as you need it to be to address the above issues. If that means writing three sentences, so be it. If you want to write a novel describing your family's history and your tormented childhood (remember, childhood does last for decades), that's fine too.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:12:56 by Steve

character classes

Forbidden Classes:

  • Cleric

  • Wizard

Note that outdoor-focused powers, abilities etc have Underdark equivalents. You could easily have a Ranger, for example, skilled at traversing the wilds of the underground and being knowledgeable in the ways of fungi and mosses instead of trees.

Note that Druids and Rangers would both require a bit of work, but we can create some underground version of each if a player really really wants to.

Prestige Classes:

  • Bellydancer

character generation

1. Before you begin, read role-playing

2. Next, see the Dark Elf racial traits and dark elf and dark elf PC sections.

3. Email Steve with an outline of the character you'd like to play. Once he's ok'ed your idea:

4. You need to create your character sheet.

  • Note: for Gestalt characters, it looks like the easiest way to do this is simply print out the blank character sheets from Hero Forge and do it manually. Let me know if you need any help with it.

    If you're more daring (or have a single-class character) Hero Forge and Spell Forge spreadsheets or the PCGen application to create your character. Hero Forge is located in the Spider Guard Yahoo! group site (check the Monster Manual option on the first tab to enable Elf, Drow):

    • http://games.groups.yahoo.com/group/spiderguard/files/

      PCGen will be posted there soon.

      eTools is similar to PCGen and I'm having better luck getting the extended datasets. Try this for now.

      Additional character sheet options are listed on the Character Sheets page.

      Excel file Drow name generator: http://underwiki.redwoodrhino.com/downloads/Drow_names.xls

5. Make a cool looking character image (totally optional)

  • (for the artistically uninclined try: http://underwiki.redwoodrhino.com/downloads/HeroMachine2.zip)

For rolling stats:

  • Roll 4d6, drop the lowest die. Repeat five times so you have a list of six stat rolls. If you don't have at least one 16 (before racial modifications), reroll all six. Assign as you like to the various stats.

Starting Equipment:

  • Take what you think is reasonable starting equipment for your character, based on their level and background.

Make sure you look at the house rules section for legal texts, virtues and flaws and other custom rules.

5. Email a copy of the proposed character sheet to Steve for approval, along with your written character background.

last edited 2005-11-08 23:49:47 by Eric

competition

Competition among darkelves is of absolutely paramount importance for individuals and the House they serve. Every darkelf house wishes to be on the City Council; if it's already there, it wishes to be higher in prominence. While the moral code stresses darkelf cooperation for survival of the race, the Rules also specifically demand the destruction of weakness, regardless of the cost.

Each individual darkelf also strives to out-maneuver peers and competitors for the choicest positions, favors and access to other leaders and opportunities. The desire for both individual and House primacy leads to intense underhanded dealings and vicious battles across every aspect of darkelf resources, from trade routes and social position to subterfuge and assassination. Houses have even been known to destroy other Houses entirely - if one House can kill all living members of a Family without witnesses from other noble families being brought to the City Council, it will go unpunished. In fact it will rise in the rankings, assuming the family was above it (and why would a House spend such resources to eliminate a weaker one?).

Naturally, darkelves go to great lengths to avoid being caught in any activities that would overtly violate the Code.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:44:25 by Steve

cooperation

Many outsiders think that the Dark Elves can't cooperate, but that is far from the truth. Each of the Chosen recognize that it is in their best interests to work together. Decades of training together and carefully planned coordination allows Dark Elf successes where more individualistic societies might fail.

As a simple example, Dark Elf ambushes rarely leave survivors - every contingency has been foreseen and accounted for, with each member of the ambush party carrying out their role perfectly.

This strong ability to cooperate does not preclude intense competition, which is encouraged by the third Rule of the moral code.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:42:34 by Steve

cramped spaces

When traveling in cramped natural tunnels and through narrow, low corridors that vary widely in diameter, it is difficult to move as quickly or fight as efficiently as normal.

hampered combat

hampered movement

create

To create a new page, simply type in the name of the page title desired surrounded as follows: 

["NewPage"]

The brackets and quotation marks are indicators for the wiki engine to create a new page link.

Save the page's changes and view it again. You'll see a new, grey link with your page's name.

Click on it.

It will take you to a new page and ask if you want to create a new, empty page.

Click on that link and it will open up a new page's text box for your content.

last edited 2005-10-26 20:02:28 by Steve

cruelty

Most players believe that Dark Elves have an insatiable hunger for death, blood and cruel treatment of others. This is incorrect. Dark Elves have the capacity for cruelty, as every other race does. However, why should a Dark Elf waste time or resources with cruelty, torture, etc?

last edited 2005-09-19 00:20:18 by Steve

dancing

Darkelves excel at dance; it expresses the natural grace of all elves, and it is a hypnotic allure to darkelf audiences. Skilled dancers are at the top of darkelf artists.

last edited 2005-09-20 18:48:28 by Steve

dark elf

The Dark Elf race is a subset of elf that lives in the caverns and tunnels of the earth. Dark Elves refer to themselves as 'Dark Elves' or 'The Chosen'; they do not use the burn epithet of 'Drow'. They are a highly organized society that is equal parts cooperation and competition. Their inherent superiority above other races has allowed them to thrive and grow at the expense of lesser beings. Naturally, this development has encouraged lesser beings to fear and hate their betters. Read more about the Dark Elf moral code.

Dark Elves live for a very long time, as do their Burn cousins. Since Dark Elves don't marry and often change partners over the course of the centuries (and the fact that males die more frequently in the normal day-to-day of Dark Elf politics), they trace their lineage through the maternal side. Over millennia, this has led to a resource preference for the females - they are significantly stronger and larger than the males, and they hold the positions of social power and authority among their communities (like that of the Matriarch).

Physically, Dark Elves are beautiful, slim people who stand 4 1/2 to 5 feet tall, with only the tallest females approaching 5 1/2 feet in height. Weight is correspondingly slight and ranges from 75 to 120 pounds. Their skin ranges from dark grey to obsidian black, with hair of white or colored hue. Dark Elves have beautiful eyes of bright colored irises surrounding enormous pupils.

Dark Elves are fully adapted to their unlit and harsh environment, with darksight, innate resistance to spells and an uncanny agility of body and mind that allows them to easily navigate the twisting rise and fall of tunnels and chimneys deep in the earth. See dark elf racial traits.

Like their Burn cousins, Dark Elves are very aesthetically sophisticated, and dedicate a significant amount of time and energy into the Arts, crafts, and performance.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:14:25 by Steve

dark elf PC

As with characters of every other race, the variety among Dark Elf characters and personae is limited only by the imagination of the player. What follows are some notes that should help you to understand some core Dark Elf traits as you design and think through the persona of your PC; I hope to add some depth to your perspective of this fascinating race, and change some misconceptions along the way. These should not be treated as absolutes - they are merely representative of the race as a whole.

See the moral code

Some Misconceptions:

  • cruelty

    barbaric

    murderous

Some Real Traits & Tensions in the Dark Elf Psyche:

  • artistic

    pragmatism

    Despisal of weakness

    ambition

    A sense of station: Arrogance & Humility

    destiny & Caution

    cooperation & competition

last edited 2005-09-20 18:50:46 by Steve

darksight

Dark Elves can see in the complete darkness of underground passages and chambers; the range of this sight is out to 120 feet. Darksight is based in the ability to distinguish between heat and cold. Printed materials are not legible with darksight - illumination is required to write or read such things.

When faced with actual illumination, Dark Elves require a short period of time (1-4 rounds) to readjust their vision before being able to see clearly. When using Darksight, they see in black and white; color is visible with illumination (typically from a candle, a lava flow or irridescent fungus).

last edited 2005-09-20 18:51:09 by Steve

destiny

Dark Elves sometimes refer to themselves as 'the Chosen'. They truly believe that their special powers and triumphant history are an indication of some divine favor, or at least a sign of primacy in the global food chain. Despite this, Dark Elves often spend an inordinate amount of time (in the perspective of shorter-lived races) planning, re-planning and plotting to account for every last possibility. They take nothing for granted.

last edited 2005-09-20 18:51:29 by Steve

drumming

Darkelf percussion is a marvel to hear; their acute hearing combined with darkelf precision and agility provide a vast tapestry of drumming and percussion music. From portable instruments all the way up to the large tahko drums, the darkelves love the rhythmic power and complexity of drumming. Drums are most often used as the musical accompaniment to dancing, and the audiences will sometimes get involved, adding clapping, slapping or whistling to the performance.

last edited 2005-09-20 18:52:22 by Steve

duergar

Duergar are the cave-dwelling cousins of burn dwarves. They are expert stoneworkers.

last edited 2005-10-26 17:55:37 by Steve

episodic play

Many games play in live, continuous action. This game will feature "episodes" that may be followed by breaks in the timeline. These breaks could last for hours, days, weeks, or even years. As the PC's complete (successfully or not) various episodes, there will likely be downtime afterwards.

The downtime can be used for a variety of things - training to a new level, traveling to a new place, resuming usual activities, or even individual actions, correspondence or adventures.

last edited 2005-09-20 18:54:16 by Steve

family

The Family of a house is the actual blood-born family whose name is used by the House - these are the nobility. Only those with the House Name can be promoted to positions of real leadership in the House. The Matriarch also has the authority to grant the House Name to other individuals in the House. This is only done under extremely rare situations, and is an irreversible decision (of course, she retains the authority to kill them if need be...).

last edited 2005-09-20 18:54:42 by Steve

feats

New Feats:

  • These are taken and modified from the Forgotten Realms Underdark and the Plot & Poison sourcebooks.

Armor Mastery (General)

You are unusually limber when wearing a type of armor you have been trained to use.

  • Prerequisite: Armor Proficiency of the necessary type.

    Benefit: Choose a kind of armor (chain shirt, scale mail, full plate, and so on). When you wear that armor, its armor check penalty is reduced by 1. ACP cannot be reduced below 0 in this way.

    This feat can be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

Armor Tumbler (General)

You can tumble when wearing armor that reduces your speed.

  • Prerequisite: Armor Mastery, Armor Proficiency (heavy), Armor Proficiency (medium), Tumble 5+ ranks.

    Benefit: You can use the Tumble skill even when your speed is reduced by armor. If your speed is reduced by the load you carry, you still cannot use the Tumble skill.

Brilliant Dancers (Dark Elf)

Your dancing lights ability can range over a wider area, and you can make more of them.

  • Prerequisite: ability to cast dancing lights as an innate ability

    Benefit: When you cast dancing lights, you can create three times the normal number of lights and you can have them range over a 30-foot radius area. When you cast the spell you can choose what form the lights take, in groups as though you cast three dancing lights spells. Thus, you could make four lanterns and eight spheres; four torches, four lanterns and a glowing figure; three glowing figures; or any other combination of the spell's effects.

Bull Rush Strike (General)

You gain an extra attack against a foe you bull rush.

  • Prerequisite: Str 13+, Improved Bull Rush, Power Attack

    Benefit: Whenever you successfully bull rush an opponent, you immediately get to attack that opponent. This does not allow you to take a full attack against that foe if you have moved more than 5 feet.

    This feat can be chosen as a bonus Fighter feat.

Cast on the Run (General)

You are trained to cast spells as you move.

  • Prerequisite: Dex 13+, Con 13+, Concentration 5+ ranks, Dodge, Mobility

    Benefit: When casting a spell with a casting time of 1 action or less, you may move both before and after you cast the spell, provided that the total distance moved is no greater than your speed. When you cast the spell, you must succeed at a Concentration check (DC 15 + spell level). On a failure, the spell does not take effect and is wasted.

Caver (General)

The Underdark's cave systems stretch for thousands of miles below the surface. You are knowledgeable about the secrets of the subterranean world and wise in its ways.

  • Benefit: You gain a +2 bonus on Heal checks and Survival checks made in the Underdark.

Color Darkvision (Dark Elf)

You can see color with your darkvision.

  • Prerequisite: Darkvision.

    Benefit: You can distinguish colors with your darkvision as though it were normal vision.

    Normal: Darkvision is black and white only.

Creature Darkness (Dark Elf)

You can cast darkness on creatures.

  • Prerequisite: Ability to use darkness as an innate ability.

    Benefit: You may cast the darkness spell on creatures as though its Target entry were creature touched. The touched creature receives a Will save to resist the effect (if desired).

Cut Arrows (General)

You can knock arrows and other projectiles from the air.

  • Prerequisite: Dex 13+, Deflect Arrows, Improved Unarmed Strike

    Benefit: When using the Deflect Arrows feat, you need not have a free hand. You can deflect ranged attacks with your feet, a weapon, or an object in your hands. If yo usuccessfully deflect the the ranged attack with a weapon, you may deal damage to the projectile that would have hit you.

    Normal: You may only use the Deflect Arrows feat if you have a free hand.

Damaging Hold (General)

You deal more damage to foes when you grapple.

  • Prerequisite: Str 13+, Improved Unarmed Strike

    Benefit: When you deal damage to a foe during a grapple (with a weapon or with unarmed strike), add 1 1/2 times your Str bonus to the damage dealt.

Dark Spell (Metamagic)

Spells you cast appear as dark as night (or as dark as the Underdark, rather).

  • Benefit: You can change the visible manifestation of a spell to an opaque black color as long as the effect would not be changed by doing so. Thus, you could cast a dark fireball, the explosion and flames of which would be black. You could not, for example, cast a dark color spray, light or wind wall spell. If the spell does not have a visual effect, summons a creature or has Personal or Target Creature(s) as its Target entry, you cannot apply this feat to it. A dark spell uses up a spell slot of the spell's normal level.

    Special: Spells modified by the Dark Spell feat are more difficult to identify. Spellcraft checks to identify the spell from observing its visible manifestation incur a -1 circumstance penalty.

Darksight (Dark Elf)

You can see normally into and beyond darkness spells.

  • Prerequisite: Darkvision, Blind-Fight, ability to cast darkness, SR 15+.

    Benefit: You see normally with your darkvision into and beyond magical darkness spells and effects (even deeper darkness), but once inside the effect's area you are affected as normal. This does not allow you to see through spells rendered dark by the Dark Spell feat. This is a supernatural ability.

Deepest Darkness (Dark Elf)

Darkness spells you cast affect a larger area than normal.

  • Prerequisite: Ability to cast darkness innately.

    Benefit: When you cast a darkness spell, it can have a radius of up to 60 feet. You decide the radius when you cast the spell, and it remains the same for the spell's duration.

    Special: If you have the Distant Darkness feat and/or the Creature Darkness feat, you may apply either or both of these feats to the expanded-radius darkness spell.

Desperate Blow (General)

You can focus all your energy into a single devastating attack.

  • Prerequisite: Base attack bonus +6 or higher.

    Benefit: When you could normally make several melee or ranged attacks using the full attack action, you may sacrifice all your other attacks to give yourself a bonus on one single attack. For each attack sacrificed, your primary attack gains a +2 circumstance bonus to hit and a +1 circumstance bonus to damage. Only iterative attacks gained from your base attack bonus can be sacrificed in this manner; extra attacks from the Two-Weapon Fighting or Rapid Shot feats, the flurry of blows ability, haste, and other game effects cannot be so sacrificed, nor can they be used during the round that you use Desperate Blow. Invoking this feat to make a single attack is a full-round action.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

Dextrous Grappler (General)

You grapple with an unusual deftness.

  • Prerequisite: Improved Unarmed Strike, Escape Artist 5+ ranks, base attack bonus +4 or higher.

    Benefit: When you make a grapple check, you may apply your Dexterity modifier to the roll rather than your Strength modifier.

    Normal: You apply your Strength modifier to all Grapple checks.

Distant Darkness (Dark Elf)

You can cast darkness at long range.

  • Prerequisite: Ability to cast darkness as an innate ability.

    Benefit: You may cast the darkness spell as though its Range entry read Long (400ft + 40ft / level).

    Special: If you have both the Distant Darkness and Creature Darkness feats, you may cast darkness spells as though the Target entry read Creature Touched, and at long range.

Enspelled Summons (Metamagic)

When you summon creatures, they appear with a spell you can cast already affecting them.

  • Benefit: When you cast a spell that summons a creature, choose a spell targeting the creature with a casting time of 1 action that you have prepared or for which you have an available slot. That prepared spell or spell slot is also expended when you cast the summoning spell. If the spell is one that the summoned creature can resist, it receives a saving throw and checks for spell resistance as normal. If the spell affects the summoned creature, it appears with the spell already having been in effect for 1 round.

    If the spell to affect the summoned creature requires a touch attack or ranged attack, assume you hit. If you are summoning more than one creature and want to use a spell that could affect more than one creature, assume it affects as many as possible of the summoned creatures (you touched as many as the spell allows, the maximum number of creatures were in the area, and so on). If only a certain number of the summoned creatures can be affected, you decide which ones are. An enspelled summons spell uses up a spell slot one level higher than the spell's actual level.

Exceptional Climber (General)

You climb almost as easily as you walk.

  • Prerequisite: Base Reflex save +3 or higher, Climb 5+ ranks, Skill Focus (Climb)

    Benefit: You retain half your Dexterity bonus to Armor Class when climbing. In addition, you gain a +2 competence bonus on all checks to Climb at an accelerated rate.

    Normal: You lose your Dexterity bonus while climbing.

Exceptional Tumbler (General)

You tumble almost as easily as you walk.

  • Prerequisite: Base Reflex save +3 or higher, Tumble 5+ ranks, Skill Focus (Tumble)

    Benefit: You can use the Tumble skill to move any distance up to your speed +10 feet during a round. You can also tumble when making the Charge or Run actions; doing so adds +5 to the DC of any Tumble checks you make as part of your movement.

    Normal: You can only tumble 20 feet and only as part of normal movement.

Exchange Component (Metamagic)

You can switch the components of a spell.

  • Benefit: If a spell normally has a verbal component but not a somatic component, or vice versa, you may switch the required component to the type it does not have - somatic or verbal. Essentially, spells you cast that do not have one of the two aforementioned component types can have either at your discretion. Spellcasters who prepare their spells must choose which type of component the spell has when preparing the spell. A spell with exchanged components uses up a spell slot of the spell's normal level. You cannot exchange the components of a spell altered by metamagic feats such as Silent Spell.

Far Hand (Metamagic)

You can use touch spells as though you had reach.

  • Benefit: When yuo cast a touch-range spell, you can use it on foes as though your reach were 5 feet greater than it is. You need not physically touch the target of the spell, but must still make a melee touch attack. You must have line of effect to the target to affect it with the spell. When holding the charge of an offensive spell, you threaten spaces as though you had the extended reach. A far hand spell uses up a spell slot of the spell's normal level.

Fatal Fire (Dark Elf)

Your faerie fire spells deal damage.

  • Prerequisite: Ability to cast faerie fire as an innate ability.

    Benefit: When you cast the faerie fire spell, creatures in its area take 1d4 points of fire damage plus 1 point per level (max +5). Affected creatures receive a Reflex save to take half damage, but they are still outlined by the normal effects of the spell.

    Special: You can use this feat with the Wide Fire feat to deal damage to creatures in up to a 20-foot radius area.

Genius Skill (General)

You have a stunning ability with a particular skill.

  • Prerequisite: Skill Focus (selected skill), 5+ ranks (selected skill)

    Benefit: Choose one skill you can assign ranks to. In addition to the normal key ability for that skill, you apply the modifier for another ability, chosen from teh list of equivalents below:

    Strength: Dexterity or Constitution

    Dexterity: Intelligence or Wisdom

    Constitution: Dexterity or Charisma

    Intelligence: Wisdom

    Wisdom: Intelligence

    Charisma: Intelligence or Wisdom

    Special: You can take this feat more than once. Each time, it must apply to a new skill. Note that the equivalency list above is designed to work with skills listed in the core rulebooks. Check with your GM to make sure that the ability you choose is appropriate for the affected skill.

Grappling Threat (General)

You threaten adjacent spaces when you are grappling.

  • Prerequisites: Dextrous Grappler, Improved Unarmed Strike, Escape Artist 5+ ranks, base attack bonus +4 or higher.

    Benefit: When you are grappling, you still threaten adjacent spaces. You can attack foes not involved in the grapple, using unarmed strikes or any melee weapon you can wield while grappled, but you incur a -10 circumstance penalty on those attack rolls. You still do not threaten adjacent spaces when pinned.

    Normal: You do not threaten adjacent spaces while grappling.

Great Pierce (General)

You wield ranged weapons with such skill that you can endanger multiple foes with one attack.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Pierce, Point Blank Shot, Precise Shot

    Benefit: As Pierce (see that entry), except that your ranged attack may continue on to the next creature in line and in range indefinitely, so long as you down each creature in turn.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

Highborn Dark Elf (General)

You have learned how to tap into the advanced magical abilities available to you through your noble heritage.

  • Prerequisites: dark elf, This feat can only be taken at level 1.

    Benefit: You may use detect magic and levitate once per day, with a caster level equal to your character level.

Impressive Battledance (General)

You can easily daze foes with your dizzying battledance.

  • Prerequisites: Perform 5+ ranks, Perform (battledance)

    Benefit: You can use the Perform (battledance) skill in combat as a standard action to cause your foes to become dazed.

    Normal: Using Perform (battledance) in combat is a full-round action.

Impressive Demonstration (General)

You can intimidate foes in combat with disturbing ease.

  • Prerequisites: Intimidate 5+ ranks

    Benefit: You can use the Intimidate skill in combat as a move-equivalent action to cause your foes to become shaken.

    Normal: Using Intimidate in combat is a standard action.

Impressive Flourish (General)

You can easily dazzle foes with your stunning prowess.

  • Prerequisites: Perform 5+ ranks, Perform (attack flourish)

    Benefit: Once per round you can use the Perform (attack flourish) skill in combat as a free action to cause your foes to become dazzled.

    Normal: Using Perform (attack flourish) in combat is a move-equivalent action.

Improved Combat Reflexes (General)

You exploit all of your foe's mistakes.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Combat Reflexes

    Benefit: You may make several attacks of opportunity against the same foe, each time that opponent provokes one during the round. You still have a maximum number of attacks of opportunity equal to 1 + your Dexterity bonus.

    Normal: The Combat Reflexes feat allows you to make several attacks of opportunity, but you cannot make more than one attack of opportunity per foe during that round.

Improved Deflect Arrows (General)

You can deflect many ranged attacks.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Combat Reflexes, Deflect Arrows, Improved Unarmed Strike

    Benefit: When using the Deflect Arrows feat, you may deflect a number of ranged attacks per round equal to 1 + your Dexterity bonus.

    Normal: You may use the Deflect Arrows feat only once per round.

Improved Levitation (General)

You have learned how to use only part of your levitate ability at a time, allowing multiple uses with shorter durations.

  • Prerequisites: Levitate as a spell-like ability

    Benefit: You may use your levitate ability in 10-minute increments instead of using the entire duration at once. The number of times per day that you may use the levitate at the shorter duration is equal to your character level.

Increased Spell Resistance (General)

Your spell resistance is better than average.

  • Prerequisites: Spell resistance, base attack bonus +2 or higher

    Benefit: You have a spell resistance +2 higher than normal.

Invisible Spell (Metamagic)

Spells you cast can be made invisible.

  • Prerequisites: Traceless Spell, ability to cast 2nd-level spells

    Benefit: You can make the visible manifestation of a spell invisible as long as the effect would not be changed by doing so. Thus, you could cast an invisible fireball, the explosion and flames of which would be invisible (although the light created by the flash would be visible). You could not, for example, cast an invisible color spray or light spell. If the spell does not have a visual effect, summons a creature or has Personal or Target Creature(s) as its Target entry, you cannot apply this feat to it. This is an invisibility effect. An invisible spell uses up a spell slot two levels higher than the spell's actual level.

    Special:Although it is obvious to anyone observing you that you cast a spell, this feat allows you to cast spells (even from hiding) without automatically being revealed as their source. Spells modified by the Invisible Spell feat can be more difficult to identify. Spellcraft checks to identify the spell from observing its visible manifestation incur a -10 circumstance penalty.

Lightning Grab (General)

You are an expert at disarming and disabling foes.

  • Prerequisites: Int 13+, Combat Expertise, Improved Disarm

    Benefit: After successfully disarming an opponent, you can immediately make a free attempt to grab that opponent to initiate a grapple. Attempting to start a grapple in this way does not provoke an attack of opportunity.

Lightsight (Dark Elf)

You are adapted to bright light.

  • Benefit: When abruptly exposed to bright light (such as a daylight spell) you are not blinded, nor do you suffer any penalty while operating in bright light. You are still affected normally by spell or environmental effects based on bright light that would blind or hamper a creature without light blindness. This spell does not eliminate damage due to light effects (such as searing light) - only blindness and penalties on attacks, saves and checks.

    Normal: When abruptly exposed to bright light, dark elves are blinded for 1 round and suffer a -1 circumstance penalty on attack rolls, saves and checks while operating in bright light.

Lingering Touch (Metamagic)

You can cast spells while holding a charged touch spell.

  • Prerequisites: ability to cast touch-range spells

    Benefit: When you cast a touch-range spell, you can hold the charge even if you cast other spells before discharging the effect. If you cast another touch-range spell, both spells can be retained until you touch a target or targets according to the normal rules for holding a charge, but casting another spell when holding two charges causes both held spells to dissipate without effect. Touching any creature or object causes both spells to affect the target touched. The target has the normal opportunities to resist both spells.

    Normal: When you cast a touch-range spell, you cannot cast another spell without losing the charge.

Moving Spell (Metamagic)

You can make stationary spells move to your will.

  • Prerequisites: This feat can only be applied to a spell with a stationary area of effect and a duration of more than 1 round. Each round, you can move the affected spell's effect up to 20 feet as a standard action by making a successful Concentration check (DC 20 + spell level). You can move the effect in any direction desired, despite prevailing winds and other environmental factors, so long as there is a line of effect from you to all points in the path of the spell and the desired location is not out of the spell's range for you.

    If a creature would be released from the effects of a spell by moving out of the area of effect, moving the effect off of a creature also releases it. For example, moving a reverse gravity spell away from a creature would cause it to fall. Creatures cannot be moved by moving a spell effect unless the spell's normal effect would move them. Moving the spell effect cannot cause a creature to be affected by the spell more than once during a round.

    Certain spells rely on stationary objects to have an effect or to anchor their effects, such as entangle and web. These spells can only be moved if the required objects are present along the entire path of the spell effect's movement.

    A moving spell uses up a spell slot three levels higher than the spell's actual level.

Nullify Enemy Magic (Metamagic)

You can have your spells dispel or suppress magic cast only by enemies.

  • Benefit: When you cast a spell modified by this feat that dispels or suppresses magic (antimagic field, disjunction, dispel magic, globe of invulnerability, greater dispelling, minor globe of invulnerability, and so on), it affects only spells and effects from creatures you perceive as foes. A spell that nullifies enemy magic uses up a spell slot four levels higher than the actual spell level.

Nullify Magic Type (Metamagic)

You can control what sort of magic your spells dispel or suppress.

  • Benefit: Choose one type of magic: arcane or divine. When you cast a spell modified by this feat that dispels or suppresses magic (antimagic field, disjunction, dispel magic, globe of invulnerability, greater dispelling, minor globe of invulnerability, and so on), it affects only spells and effects of that type. A spell that nullifies a magic type uses up a spell slot two levels higher than the spell's actual level.

Nullify School (Metamagic)

You can have your spells dispel or suppress magic from a specific school.

  • Benefit: Choose one school of magic. When you cast a spell modified by this feat that dispels or suppresses magic (antimagic field, disjunction, dispel magic, globe of invulnerability, greater dispelling, minor globe of invulnerability, and so on), it affects only spells and effects of that school. A spell that nullifies magic of a school uses up a spell slot of the spell's normal level.

Painful Pin (General)

You force opponents into painful positions when you pin them.

  • Prerequisites: Improved Unarmed Strike, base attack bonus +4 or higher

    Benefit: When you pin a foe during a grapple, the creature must make a successful Fortitude save (DC 10 + 1/2 your character level + your Strength modifier) or be dazed for 1d4 rounds. A dazed creature can take no actions (although it can defend itself normally).

Perfect Shot (General)

You are adept at finding the most beneficial place to strike an opponent with a ranged attack.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Weapon Proficiency (selected ranged weapon), Point Blank Shot, Precise Shot, Weapon Focus (selected ranged weapon), base attack bonus +3 or higher.

    Benefit: When wielding the selected ranged weapon, you may add your Dexterity modifier instead of your Strength modifier to damage rolls, even if the ranged weapon is not mighty. If you cannot normally apply your Strength modifier to damage (such as when using a crossbow), you can still apply your Dexterity modifier.

    Your target must be within 30 feet, This feat does not help you when attacking creatures that are immune to critical hits - apply your Strength modifier (if normally allowed) to the damage roll as normal.

    You can use this feat with a melee weapon, but you can apply your Dexterity modifier to damage rolls only when you throw that weapon.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Special: You can gain this feat multiple times. Each time you take this feat, you must apply it to a new weapon.

Perfect Strike (General)

You are adept at finding the most effective place to strike an opponent in melee.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Weapon Proficiency (selected melee weapon), Weapon Finesse (selected melee weapon), Weapon Focus (selected ranged weapon), base attack bonus +3 or higher.

    Benefit: When wielding the selected melee weapon, you may add your Dexterity modifier instead of your Strength modifier to damage rolls. This feat does not help you when attacking creatures that are immune to critical hits; apply your Strength modifier to the damage roll as normal.

    When you make off-hand attacks with the selected weapon, add one-half your Dexterity modifier to damage instead of one-half your Strength modifier. However, when you make two-handed attacks with the selected weapon, you only add your Dexterity modifier to damage, not 1 1/2 times your Dexterity modifier. This feat cannot be applied to thrown weapon attacks.

    This feat can be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Special: You can gain this feat multiple times. Each time you take this feat, you must apply it to a new weapon.

Pierce (General)

You can send ranged weapon attacks through a target you kill, possibly striking a nearby foe.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Point Blank Shot, Precise Shot

    Benefit: If you deal enough damage to an opponent with a ranged weapon to make it drop (typically by damaging it to below 0 hit points), the attack can pass through that opponent, possibly striking another creature behind it. The second creature must be directly behind the foe you downed along a straight line between you and the original target, within the weapon's range. Make a normal ranged attack at the same bonus as the attack that downed the previous creature, taking into account any new range penalty, cover (the downed foe does not count), and concealment. If you hit, you deal damage as normal.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

Ranged Weapon Channel (Metamagic)

You can use a particular ranged weapon to channel your touch-range spells.

  • Prerequisites: Far Hand, Weapon Focus (selected ranged weapon)

    Benefit: You can deliver touch-range spells through attacks with the selected ranged weapon. You must have the weapon or ammunition in hand when you cast the spell. This does not imbue the weapon or its ammunition with the spell; if you drop either or give either to another character, the spell is wasted. You must make a normal ranged attack roll instead of a touch attack to deliver the spell, and if you hit, the attack must deal damageat least equal to the spell's level or the spell is wasted. The spell follows the normal rules for touch spells, so it is not dissipated by a missed attack, it can affect multiple targets, and you can hold the charge for the spell's duration. A ranged weapon channel spell uses up a spell slot of the spell's normal level.

    Special: If you have the Lingering Touch feat, you can channel two touch spells into the ranged weapon.

Reconcentrate (General)

You can renew spell effects after you have ceased concentrating on them.

  • Prerequisites: Ability to cast 2nd-level spells, Concentration 5+ ranks, Combat Casting

    Benefit: When yuo voluntarily end concentrating on a spell effect, you may attempt to renew concentrating on it up to a number of rounds later equal to your caster level. This can cause the spell to take effect again. To renew the spell, make a Concentration check (DC 15 + spell level + number of rounds since you last succesfully concentrated on the spell). On a success, the spell effect renews.

    A renewed spell takes effect as though you had not stopped concentrating, but creatures affected by the original spell are only affected if they are again in its area of effect, and they can make new saving throws to avoid or lessen the spell's effect as normal. You cannot change the placement or shape of a spell effect, such as a wall of fire, nor can you renew the effect if you are out of range to cast the spell in its original location or are otherwise unable to control the effect.

    This feat can affect only spells that have Concentration listed as part of their Duration entry. You cannot extend a spell effect's duration beyond the normal limit. For example, a spell with a duration of "Concentration, up to 1 round/level" could not be renewed by a fifth level spell caster 6 rounds after casting.

Savant Skill (General)

You have a surprising knack for a particular skill.

  • Prerequisites: Skill Focus (selected skill)

    Benefit: Choose one skill you can assign ranks to. Any ability score penalty you would suffer when using that skill does not apply.

Shield Mastery (General)

You are trained to use a shield with extraordinary deftness.

  • Prerequisites: Shield Proficiency

    Benefit: Choose a type of shield (buckler, small, large or tower). When you use that type of shield, its armor check penalty is reduced by 1. ACP penalties cannot be reduced below 0.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Special: You can gain this feat multiple times. Its effects do not stack. Each time you take the feat, it applies to a new type of shield.

Shield Specialization (General)

You can use a shield to attack as well as you can use a weapon.

  • Prerequisites: Shield Proficiency, Shield Mastery

    Benefit: When you make a shield bash attack with a type of shield selected for the Shield Mastery feat, you can regain the shield's armor bonus to your AC as a free action. If you choose the buckler for this feat, you can make shield bash attacks with it that deal 1d3 damage (x2 critical) and do not suffer the normal -1 penalty on off-hand weapon attacks, whether with weapons or shield bashes. In addition, you can regain the buckler's AC bonus after making an attack with an off-hand weapon.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Normal: When you make a shield bash attack, you lose the shield's AC bonus until your next action.

    Special: You can gain this feat multiple times. Its effects do not stack. Each time you take the feat, it applies to a new type of shield.

Soundsight (General)

You gain blindsight, similar to that of a bat, within a short range.

  • Prerequisites: Alertness, Blind-Fight, Skill Focus (Listen)

    Benefit: Due to your exceptional hearing and understanding of sound, you gain blindsight to a range of 10 feet. In addition you do not normally need to make a Spot or Listen check to notice creatures within the range of your blindsight.

    A silence spell blocks your blindsight, and any abrupt exposure to a very loud sound that originates from within the range of your blindsight (sound burst, shout, fireball, an exploding thunderstone, etc) deafens you and suppresses your blindsight for 1 round. When the source fo a continuous very loud sound (a roaring waterfall, dwarven foundry, tornado and the like) is within range of your blindsight, you suffer a -1 circumstance penalty on attack rolls, saves and checks.

Spring Charge (General)

You can charge when making a spring attack.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, Dodge, Mobility, Spring Attack, base attack bonus of +6 or higher.

    Benefit: While making a spring attack, if you move in a straight line toward your target and move more than 10 feet before the attack, you may choose to treat this as a charge. You gain the normal +2 bonus on your attack roll for charging, and suffer the normal -2 penalty to your AC for 1 round.

    This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

Strong Mind (General)

You are unusually difficult to affect with psionic powers and mind attacks.

  • Prerequisites: base Will save +4

    Benefit: You gain a +3 bonus on saving throws against psionic abilities and mind blast attacks, as well as any supernatural ability that uses sheer mental force to stun or disable an opponent.

Strong Off-Hand Attack (General)

Your off-hand attacks are as strong as attack rolls with your preferred hand.

  • Prerequisites: Str 15+, Dex 15+, Ambidexterity

    Benefit: You add your full Strength bonus to damage dealt by your off-hand attacks. This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Normal: You add 1/2 of your Strength bonus to damage dealt by your off-hand attacks.

    Special: Creatures with multiple secondary attacks that take this feat add their full Strength bonus to damage dealt by all those attacks.

Strong Spellcasting (General)

Your spells are more difficult to dispel.

  • Prerequisites: When someone other than yourself tries to dispel any of your spells, the dispel check has a DC of 13 + your caster level.

    Normal: Dispel checks against a spell have a DC of 11 + the spell's caster level.

Strong Two-Handed Attack (General)

Your attacks with a two-handed weapon are especially devastating.

  • Prerequisites: Str 15+, Dex 15+

    Benefit: When wielding a weapon two-handed, you add double your Strength bonus to damage dealt by that weapon. This feat may be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Normal: You add 1 1/2 times your Strength bonus to damage dealt by your two-handed weapon attacks.

Total Darkvision (Dark Elf)

You can see as far with your darkvision as a human can with normal vision.

  • Prerequisites: Alertness, Skill Focus (Spot), darkvision 120 ft.

    Benefit: The range of your darkvision is not limited to any specific distance; you can see as far as a human in daylight. This is a supernatural ability, so your darkvision is reduced to its natural range in an antimagic field or under similar circumstances.

Traceless Spell (General)

You can cast spells so that noone can trace a line back to you.

  • Prerequisites: Ability to cast 2nd-level spells

    Benefit: You can modify spells that are visible as they travel from you to the target, targets or targeted area. The spell still follows the normal line of effect but is not visible as it does so. This feat cannot be applied to spells that project out from you as an area of effect. Thus you can mask the path of magic missile, fireball or ray of enfeeblement, but not to hide lightning bolt or cone of cold. This is an invisibility effect. A traceless spell uses up a spell slot one level higher than the actual spell level.

    Special: Although it is obvious to anyone observing you that you cast a spell, this feat allows you to cast spells (even from hiding) without automatically being revealed as their source. Spellcraft checks to identify the spell from observing its effect incur a -1 circumstance penalty.

Tunnelfighter (General)

You can fight more naturally in the cramped and close quarters of caves and tunnels than usual.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13 or Tunnelrunner feat

    Benefit: ou ignore the penalty for hampered combat when fighting with light or one-handed weapons in a narrow space (an area shorter than but at least half of your space) or a low space (an area shorter than but at least one-half of your height). Furthermore, you take only a -4 circumstance penalty when using a two-handed weapon in such conditions. In a space both narrow and low, you function as if only one of those conditions applied. In addition, when fighting in cramped quarters, you do not lose your Dexterity bonus to Armor Class.

    Normal: In a narrow or low space, a creature without this feat takes a -2 circumstance penalty on attack rolls with light weapons and a -4 circumstance penalty on attack rolls with one-handed weapons. It cannot use two-handed weapons at all. Such a creature also loses its Dexterity bonus to AC. In a space that is both narrow and low, the penalties are doubled.

Tunnelrunner (General)

You can move naturally in the cramped quarters of caves and tunnels.

  • Benefit: You ignore the speed reduction for hampered movement when moving in a narrow space (an area shorter than but at least half of your space) or a low space (an area shorter than but at least one-half of your height). In a space both narrow and low, you function as if only one of those conditions applied. In addition, when fighting in cramped quarters, you do not lose your Dexterity bonus to Armor Class.

    Normal: In a narrow or low space, a creature without this feat is reduced to one-half normal speed and loses its Dexterity bonus to AC. In a space that is both narrow and low, speed is reduced to one-quarter normal.

Uncanny Evasion (General)

Your ability to evade certain dangerous attacks is astonishing.

  • Prerequisites: Dex 13+, evasion, improved evasion

    Benefit: When exposed to any effect that normally allows a Reflex save for half damage, you take only one quarter on a failed save.

    Normal: Improved Evasion allows you to take half damage on a failed Reflex save.

Use Magic Device Item Focus (General)

You are particularly talented at activating certain magic items.

  • Prerequisites: Use Magic Device 5+ ranks, Skill Focus (Use Magic Device)

    Benefit: Choose a particular type of magic item, such as wands or scrolls. You gain a +4 competence bonus on Use Magic Device checks to activate that type of magic item.

    Special: You can gain this feat multiple times. Its effects do not stack. Each time you take this feat, it applies to a new type of magic item.

Weapon Channel

You can use a particular melee weapon to channel your touch-range spells.

  • Prerequisites: Far Hand, Weapon Focus (selected melee weapon)

    Benefit: You can deliver touch-range spells with the selected melee weapon. You must have the weapon in hand when you cast the spell. This feat does not imbue the weapon with the spell; if you drop the weapon, throw it, or give it to another character, the spell is wasted. You must make a normal melee touch attack roll instead of a touch attack to deliver the spell, and if you hit, the attack must deal damage equal to the spell's level or the spell is wasted. The spell follows the normal rules for touch spells, so it is not dissipated by a missed attack, it can affect multiple targets, and you can hold the charge for the duration of the spell.

    Special: If you have the Lingering Touch feat, you can channel two touch spells into the weapon.

Weapon of Choice (General)

Your skill with a weapon makes it seem feather-light in your hands.

  • Prerequisites: Weapon Proficiency (selected weapon), Weapon Focus (selected weapon), base attack bonus +4 or higher.

    Benefit: Choose one weapon of a size category equal to your own, such as a scimitar (medium-sized) for a dark elf (medium-sized). You treat this weapon as a light weapon for purposes of two-weapon fighting, and you can select it for the Weapon Finesse feat. You can even use it in a grapple or when swallowed by a creature.

    This feat can be chosen as a Fighter bonus feat.

    Special: You can gain this feat multiple times. Its effects do not stack. Each time you take this feat, it applies to a new weapon.

Whisper Spell

You can whisper the verbal components of spells.

  • Benefit: When casting a spell with a verbal component, you have little chance of being overheard. Creatures can make a Listen check (DC 20 + 1 per 10 feet of distance to you) to hear your verbal components. Failure means the listener did not hear you casting the spell. Making a SpellCraft check to identify the spell as you cast it requires the observer to either hear the verbal component or see the somatic component.

    Special: Spells that rely on a creature hearing the verbal component of the spell are not effective unless the creature can hear you.

Wide Fire (Dark Elf)

Your faerie fire spells affect a larger area.

  • Prerequisites: Ability to cast faerie fire as an innate ability.

    Benefit: When you cast the faerie fire spell, it affects up to a 20-foot radius. You decide the radius when you cast the spell.

    Special: You can use this feat with the Fatal Fire feat to deal damage to creatures in a 20-foot radius area.

females

Females are the important gender in the dark elf world. They are larger, stronger and morally superior to males.

gestalt

Gestalt characters are outlined in the Unearthed Arcana book. The basic concept is that players can create a multi-class character that is a true combination of two classes. Each time you level, you get the benefits of both classes (e.g. spells and feats), and also take the more powerful improvement rate for saves, attacks, etc.

The downside is that you will suffer a significant experience point penalty; your character will count as 3 levels higher than actual when the DM calculates combat experience point awards. You can check out the http://www.d20srd.org website for more information - use the Encounter Calculator on the right.

gestalt details shows the full information on this powerful character option.

Gestalt Rulings summarizes important DM Rulings on Gestalt issues.

last edited 2005-11-26 21:55:25 by Steve

gestalt details

To make a 1st level Gestalt character, choose two standard D&D classes (also referred to as Core classes). You can also choose any of the variant Core classes available in the campaign. Build your character according to the guidelines below.

Hit Dice

Choose the larger Hit Die. For example, a monk/sorcerer would use d8 as her hit die.

Base Attack Bonus

Choose the better progression from the two classes.

Base Saving Throw Bonuses

For each save bonus (i.e. Fort, Ref, Will), choose the better progression from the two classes. For example, a 1st level gestalt fighter/wizard would have base saving throw bonuses of Fort +2, Ref +0, Will +2 -- taking the good Fort save from the fighter class and the good Will save from the wizard class.

Class Skills

Take the number of skill points gained per level from whichever class grants more skill points, and consider any skill on either skill list as a class skill for the gestalt character. Do not add up the amount of skill points gained from both classes, just take the higher amount. For example, a gestalt barbarian/bard would gain skill points per level equal to 6 + INT mod (and of course have four times this amount at 1st level), and can purchase skills from both the barbarian and bard lists as class skills.

Class Features

A gestalt character gains the class features of both classes. A 1st level gestalt rogue/cleric, for example, gets sneak attack +1d6, trapfinding, ability to cast 1st level cleric spells, and the ability to turn or rebuke undead. Class and ability based restrictions (such as arcane spell failure chance for wizards and a druid's prohibition on wearing metal armor) apply normally to a gestalt character, no matter what the other class is.

Progression

A gestalt character follows a similar procedure when he attains 2nd and subsequent character levels. Each time he gains a new level, he chooses two classes, takes the best aspects of each, and applies them to his characteristics. A few caveats apply, however. Class features that two classes share (such as uncanny dodge) accrue at the rate of the faster class. Do not combine or stack them in any way, as you can with similar features from prestige classes. Gestalt characters with more than one spellcasting class keep track of their spells per day seperately. A gestalt character cannot combine two prestige classes at any level, though its okay to combine a prestige class and a core class. And as always, you may select two core classes instead of opting for the use of prestige classes. Gestalt characters must also adhere to the prerequisites needed to take prestige classes, though on the whole they are able to fulfill such prerequisites earlier on in their careers. Pay attention to alignment based features and restrictions when building your gestalt character. For example, combining monk and barbarian would be self-defeating as monks have to be lawful, and barbarians lose their ability to Rage if they become lawful.

Shamefully stolen from http://ericheitzman.com/wiki/index.php/Gestalt_Characters, who shamelessly stole it from http://www.angelfire.com/rpg/drowcampaign/gestalt.html, who in turn shamelessly stole the material from Unearthed Arcana without citation.

guard

The Guard protect the family and the house resources. They are also used in inter-House conflicts and in times of expansion and development into new areas.

healing

When you rest, add your constitution bonus to hit points regained.

Rates of Healing:

full 8 hours rest: 1 hp * (level + con bonus)

full day of rest: 2 hp * (level + con bonus)

house

A 'House' is the largest unit of social organization in dark elf society. Each House strives for dominance over its competitors in such a way that it doesn't break the moral code - or at least doesn't get caught doing so.

A House Name can also be used in place of a Family member's name. For example, any Family member of House Oussund could simply be referred to as 'Oussund'.

Hierarchy: Each House is ruled by the Matriarch and comprised of the family, the membership, the service and the guard.

  • Rank:

    The Matriarch is absolute law;

    family is higher than

    membership is higher than

    service and guard

Note that slaves and other Animals (like lizards, spiders and farmed water animals) are property.

last edited 2006-03-30 12:37:24 by Steve

house rules

Campaign House Rules

If you can find a rule in the legal texts or in these House Rules, you can use it. Note that there are House Rules that disallow certain spells, feats, etc. This website trumps the books. Note that if there's some ability or feat that really fits your character, you can type it up and add it here, with Steve's permission.

Here are the major DM Rulings for this campaign.

last edited 2006-03-30 12:49:08 by Steve

indentured

When a dark elf incurs significant debt to the house, they may become indentured (willingly or not).

The form of indenture is up to the judging house superior.

Some examples:

  • enslaved for a period of several years

  • forced to do menial labor or degrading tasks for own group or the superior

  • demoted

  • forced to repay inflated loan with interest in an impossibly short time

last edited 2005-09-23 16:13:07 by Steve

iocaine

It is odorless, tasteless, dissolves instantly in liquid and is among the more deadly poisons known to dark elves.

last edited 2005-10-14 00:07:03 by Barrett

jewelry

Darkelves of both sexes often adorn themselves in a wide variety of jewelry - necklaces, rings, earrings, lip rings, nose rings, bracelets, armbands, pins, headbands, etc. Darkelves are very skilled at the various crafts required to design and make very fine jewelry of all kinds. They often prize svirfneblin gemcutters, as no race is as good at drawing the best from each and every stone as they.

The only times that darkelves are not so decorated are when stealth is needed or combat is imminent. An unexpected meeting with unadorned darkelves would be very undesirable.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:04:32 by Steve

legal texts

For the purposes of this campaign, any feat, skill, spell, rule, etc from the Player's Handbook, Expanded Psionics Handbook or Dungeon Master's Guide is fair game.

If you wish to add something in, consult the DM.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:04:50 by Steve

life at Nerr'tenden

Inhabitants at Nerr’tenden are relatively comfortable, considering the distance from Dolthgurdar. There is a small tea house and a modest but comfortable bath and spa chamber fed from the springs. The Steward has insisted upon maintaining the amenities of civilized life, with gatherings for music, sculpture and tea. Skilled cooks provide quality meals (for the dark elves), while the bath master relaxes the mind and body of Nerr’tenden’s residents with her ministrations and scented oils. While the accommodations are not luxurious by any stretch of the imagination, Nerr’tenden is a comfortable place to plot ascendance.

last edited 2006-03-30 16:00:57 by Steve

light blindness

Abrupt exposure to bright light (such as sunlight or a daylight spell) blinds dark elves for 1 round. In subsequent rounds, dark elves are dazzled as long as they remain within the affected area.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:05:13 by Steve

males

Males are subordinate to females in this matriarchal culture. They are also physically smaller and morally inferior. See dark elf.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:07:30 by Steve

marketplace

The Dolthgurdar marketplace is a dynamic and powerful confluence of goods, money and ambition. Several dozen commodity goods and crafts are traded daily at the marketplace. Caravans from the mining and farming outposts bring in enough trade to support the region's population of nearly 115,000 full-time residents and slaves.

The First House guards the trade goods and oversees trade at the marketplace.

last edited 2006-03-30 13:15:41 by Steve

membership

The Membership of a house are the tradespeople who provide the day-to-day expertise in the House's operations; they are typically promoted to this level from the service or the guard, and hold roles of day-to-day authority in areas like trade, security, etc.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:08:04 by Steve

metalworking

Metal is used in a wide variety of items in darkelf life - from wrought gates to swords, utensils and ornaments. Metalworking brings out the beauty in each object. Much like sculpture, this permanent record of artisan perspective is valued highly by the darkelf community.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:08:22 by Steve

moral code

The Dark Elves have a very strong, very simple set of core rules that have helped them to survive, and even thrive, in the hostile and challenging world they inhabit. These rules are tightly bound into the racial identity of all Dark Elves, giving them a clear sense of community, sisterhood and superiority over all others.

The Rules:

  1. Do Nothing that Harms the Dark Elf Cause

  2. Serve the Dark Elf Race as You Serve Yourself

  3. Destroy or Dominate Weakness

There is usually but a single punishment for violation: Death. In lenient situations (or privately judged situations), the offender might merely be enslaved or indentured.

Any senior member of a Dark Elf's house has authority and is responsible for judging and meting out punishment. Only the City Council can judge a House Council.

last edited 2005-09-24 03:17:20 by Steve

mortality

Nobody likes to see their character die. However, as you go through your adventures, it is likely that you will face one peril or another; at some point, characters face their final moments.

If your PC is devout and feels that bothering their deity is likely to yield aid instead of divine annoyance, the PC can call out for godly assistance - the chance of success is quite small, but it's there.

For others, or for those whose deity turned away in the critical moment, here's how to think about mortality:

Dark elves are long-lived and skilled with magic. They are also very pragmatic. If your superiors in your house think that you are worth more to them alive than dead than they will consider returning you to life, IF the appropriate spell is handy, IF they feel your death was undeserved and IF they feel like it.

However, if you don't have the ability to repay them for their troubles, you are likely to become indentured for some period of time and/or required to complete some significant task.

To Summarize:

Dying is a bad thing - it's painful on the way out, you get penalized in the game, and then your life is hell when you come back.

Try not to get killed.

last edited 2005-09-23 15:44:07 by Steve

murderous

Dark Elves are often assumed to be on the lookout for gleeful killing sprees at all times. This is far from the truth. A Dark Elf would not waste their time with killing unless it gained something specifically desired - killing is a lot of work and requires a lot of thought:

In order for a killing to be useful, many details need to be thought through: should the body be found or not? If so, when and by whom and for what purpose and under what circumstances? If not, why not, and should the fact be discovered later or not, etc? Regardless of these, what are the next actions that should be taken?

last edited 2005-09-20 19:09:10 by Steve

music

Darkelves have very keen ears, and enjoy music of all kinds. Chambers may be sculpted to provide appropriate acoustics for all different kinds of musical performances. The most popular of all is drumming, although singing and instrumental music are also very common.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:09:40 by Steve

norzzen

Norzzen moss is used to make tea of such clear and delicate flavor that it is said to be impossible to poison.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:10:19 by Steve

orogs

Orogs are essentially big orcs with some ogre blood in them. They are of average intelligence (meaning 9-12, not 'average for an orc'), and average 6 feet tall (huge compared to a dark elf). When they can be controlled and kept in line, they make good laborers.

last edited 2005-09-23 16:02:26 by Steve

poison

Poisons are a common weapon in the dark elf arsenal. From common poisons like 'sleep juice' (used in ambushes, served on crossbow quarrels) to horrifically lethal or crippling toxins appropriate for ending a bloody vendetta, poisons are a weapon of choice.

last edited 2005-09-20 21:55:04 by Steve

pragmatism

Living in the depths of the earth is a difficult existence. The intense and continual presence of competition among the Dark Elves also reinforces the need for creative thrift. As individuals and as a race, Dark Elves have learned to be pragmatic and efficient in their every action.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:10:49 by Steve

psionics

Psionics are allowed in this game, although they are uncommon. It is important to note that we will be playing without 'transparency' between magic and psionics.

This means that psionic powers do not affect magic powers, and vice versa. For example, detect psionics will not reveal magic dweomers.

We will be using one portion of the much-hated first edition Psionics Handbook:

  • Each discipline requires its own prime requisite stat - psionicists are not all Int-based characters:

    • Clairsentience: Wisdom

    • Metacreativity: Strength

    • Psychokinesis: Intelligence

    • Psychometabolism: Constitution

    • Pschyportation: Dexterity

    • Telepathy: Charisma

    Psionic characters use the prime requisite stat for the purposes of determining bonus power points and DC of manifested powers.

last edited 2005-11-13 19:31:13 by Steve

racial traits

These are modified from the Forgotten Realms Underdark book.

Stat Adjustments:

  • +2 Dexterity

  • -2 Constitution

  • +2 Intelligence

  • +2 Charisma

Immunities:

  • sleep spells and effects

Racial Bonuses:

  • +2 v. enchantment spells and effects

  • +2 on Will saves v. spells and spell-like abilities

  • +2 bonus to Listen, Search and Spot checks

  • passing within 5 feet of a concealed or secret door entitles the dark elf to a Search check to notice it as if they were actively looking for it

Vision:

  • a dark elf has darksight out to 120 feet

  • a dark elf suffers from light blindness

Spell Resistance:

  • 11+ character level

Spell-Like Abilities: A dark elf with Intelligence of 13 or higher can use the following spell-like abilities once per day (caster level = character level)

  • dancing lights

  • darkness

  • faerie fire

Weapon Proficiencies: A dark elf receives the following as bonus feats:

  • Martial Weapon Proficiency (rapier)

  • Martial Weapon Proficiency (short sword)

  • Exotic Weapon Proficiency (hand crossbow)

Automatic Languages:

  • Undercommon

  • Dark Elf

last edited 2005-09-28 22:34:10 by Barrett

role-playing

This campaign is going to be different than others you've taken part in. I want this to be a new experience for each of us. An important part of that is role-playing a character that is new to you. I imagine that few (if any) of you have ever roleplayed in a campaign comprised entirely of "evil" characters in an underground setting, so that is a start.

But I want to go further.

I want each and every one of you to pick a character type and personality that is new for you - that will be a challenge. It may be that you identify with the character, or that you don't. I imagine that over time, each of you will find something meaningful in your character that you can use to express yourself. Make it different. If you always play the water-spell mage, don't do it here. The same goes for personality - pick something new and interesting. This is your chance to broaden your horizons, to act as someone you never would dream of in the everyday roleplay.

The gauntlet has been thrown. Have fun!

The pysche and morals of a dark elf PC

Dark Elf character generation and CharacterSheets

roughside

The darkelves refer to unshaped areas as 'roughside'. The contrast is 'inside': developed and shaped tunnels and chambers.

sapphire

The sapphire market is a small one; these beautiful blue gems are a rare commodity. Only two mines send sapphires to the Dolthgurdar marketplace: Nerr'tenden and its more powerful competitor, Gaullidurth, owned by House Orlylyl.

sculpture

darksight doesn't allow easy appreciation of color or two-dimensional art. Sculpture, however is very much appreciated, whether it is used to adorn buildings and staircases or as free-standing art.

last edited 2005-09-20 19:13:06 by Steve

service

The Service are the staff-level people who make the house run - these are the cooks, maids, miners, laborers, slave-catchers and others who provide the services the House relies on.

skills

Bathmaster (Wis)

The skills of providing for guests in a bath house involve massage, washing, application of scented unguents and applying restful and healing salves.

A successful DC 10 check allows for improved long-term care, increasing healing by 1 hit point per day. Use of Oil of Relaxation (see Craft Bath Oils Skill) adds +5 to the roll (in addition to their normal effects on a single subject).

A successful DC 15 check provides a healthful experience, reducing fatigue by two levels and removing a number of non-lethal damage equal to the number the skill check exceeded the DC. This effort takes two hours. Use of Oils of Relaxation and Cure Minor Wounds each add +2 to the roll.

A successful DC 20 check provides a very healthful experience, reducing fatigue by two levels and healing one point of regular damage for each point the skill check exceeds the DC. This effort takes two hours. Use of Oils of Relaxation and Cure Light Wounds (normal) each add +2 to the roll.

Attempting to use bathmaster techniques outside of a bath house adds +10 to the DC required.

Craft Bath Oils (Int)

This skill allows one to create non-magical relaxing and healing oils, salves and unguents. Each attempt requires a full day of work. Attempting to create bath oils without appropriate equipment (pots for boiling water, funnels and coils for processing and extracting, etc) adds +15 to the DC required. Materials are expended whether the attempt is successful or not.

Craft Bath Oils DCs

  • Oil of:

    Healing Type

    DC

    Materials Cost

    relaxation

Interrogate (WIS)

You are adept at using torture to extract truthful information from unwilling prisoners. Use this skill in place of Bluff, Intimidate and/or Sense Motive when performing torture.

Check: To perform an interrogation, the subject must be secured in a grapple, ordinary restraints, or the bindings of a specialized torture device. The allowed frequency of performing a check varies by situation and implements used, but is usually once per round. Implements of torture typically provide a circumstance bonus to this check. Interrogation of a bound subject requires two phases: torture and questioning, as follows:

  • Torture: The DC to successfully torture a creature is 10 + the creature's level or HD. Damage done during the attempt occurs regardless of the success of this roll.

    Questioning: Once a creature is successfully tortured, you can attempt to pry the answer to one question from them. They get a Will save to resist; the DC is the skill check rolled to torture them. Successful saves require a new torture attempt before a question can be asked again. Victims get a cumulative +1 bonus to this save for each successful save they make against torture with a given implement. Any bonuses accrued don't apply to resist an implement with a higher circumstance bonus.

A torture subject may attempt to mislead the torturer during interrogation. The victim's Bluff check is opposed by the torturer's Interrogate check, which takes a -3 circumstance penalty due to the torturer's belief in the effectiveness of his methods.

If brought to 0 or fewer hit points by a device during the course of torture and subsequently healed, a torture victim doubles the circumstance bonus on the same device in further torture.

A successful Interrogate check vs. the victim's Sense Motive allows half the circumstance bonus from a torture device by threatening the subject with its use.

Try Again: Unlike normal methods of extracting information, a torturer may repeat the Interrogate check to extract information repeatedly.

Synergy: If you have 5 or more ranks in Bluff, Intimidate, or Sense Motive, each grants a +2 bonus on Interrogate checks.

last edited 2006-03-17 19:08:17 by Steve

slaves

Dark Elves are intelligent and like to make the most of scarce resources - they often will capture and enslave opponents rather than kill them. Typical sources of slaves are: other Dark Elves from destroyed houses or members of other races who were foolish enough to resist Dark Elf development and expansion into local areas.

Slaves are kept as long as they are more productive than the cost of feeding them.

last edited 2005-09-20 18:45:34 by Steve

station

Dark Elf dealings among their own kind are often tinged with arrogance and egotism; other races see nothing but arrogance, dismissal and indifference from these powerful people. When dealing with those who are more powerful, however, Dark Elves are absolutely ready to show humility. It is a sign of respect to your betters, and increases the likelihood that they will support you in exchange for some services or relationship. Dark Elves don't live long without being sensitive to their place and station compared to those around them.
